medowe hylle vale hir floures quycke thynge pale ouer ſpred cladde lyuere newe braunches bloſme wt many luſty hewe byd v fully glad lyght aſſuraūce haue fruyt behyght agayne autumpne lyſt ſhake whan vynes rypeth euery grape thus ſeaſon moſt luſty diſporte embraceth hertes newe recomforte oonly hope kynde dewe holſom fruyte ſhall bloſmes ſewe whan tyme cometh reuolucion thus may luſty freſſhe ſeaſon whan brydes ſynge theyr armonye ſame tyme panomye repayred dephebus parys brought choſen deuys thre thouſande knyghtes redy gone grece ſhyppes many one full vytayled may nede theſe ſhyppes nombre rede two twenty lyke wryte guydo without ado kynge cōmaundeth vnto eneas anthenor polydamas haſte redy make parys knyghtly vndertake ye haue herde iourney acheue tyme whan toke theyr leue pryamus ſhort concluſion sheweth effect entencion ſpecially theyr deuer done recure ſuſter exyone ye haue herde tofore telle ſhulde mater dwelle whan redy without ſoiour parys firſte lorde gouernour vyage made pryamus brother called dephebus theyr leue toke wepynge tenderly ſhyppe manfully whithout abode began dreſſe name venus goddeſſe myghty ioue toke theyr iournee hale vp anker large ſee gan ſayle haue wynde wylle water calme blandyſſhynge ſtylle without trouble boyſtous wawe coſtes gan faſt drawe grekes lande thynge lette fortune theyr cours mette grekyſſhe ſhyp myn auctour telleth thus whiche kyng menelaus towarde pryam famous ſtronge cyte vyſyte duke hye degre neſtor hyghte menelaus brother eke vnto kynge famous wyſe worthy great agamenon moſt name reputacion amonges grekes worthyneſſe menelay ſtorye bereth wytneſſe huſbonde quene eleyne ſuſter bretherne tweyne caſtor pollux whiche tolde theyr hande ſo worthy knyght holde tyme lyke theyr degre stryneſtar theyr moſte chefe cyte helde houſholde ſolempne ryall loue ſo ſpeciall wyll herte accordynge dede atwyxe two bretherhede none coude lyue alone eke mayde hermyone yonge doughter quene eleyne fayreneſſe moſte inly ſouereyne moſte paſſyngly excellynge beaute ¶and thus troyans ſaylynge ſee towarde grece amonge wawes wete auenture happed mete kynge menelaus ſaylynge theyr ſyde none lyſte pryde enquere paſſe forthe full huge pa none coude knowe aye wynde peſybly gan blowe troyan flete cauſynge whyle approche noble yle called cithera day hauen haſt may caſt anker bonde ſhyppes ſtronge lyſte nat tarye longe take lande full many luſty man arrayeng freſſhely ¶now yle paſſynge excellence temple great reuerence bylded olde foundacion moſt honoured region thorughout lande bothe fer neere feſte day aye yere yere lyke fylle reuolucion repeyrynge thyther great deuocion honour oonly venus goddeſſe grekes theyr beſyneſſe honoured moſt euery maner age gyftes bryngynge pylgrymage great offrynge ſacryfyſe vſed theyr paynem wyſe ¶for phane knele wake contryte herte theyr prayer make ſtatute gaue euery queſtion playne anſwere full ſolucion cerymonyes venus loute euery thynge doute hadde full declaracion thus grekes vpon citheron halowe feſte wt ryche great aray rytes dewe ferforth may hope fully better thryue ¶and fortune whan dyde aryue vp lande aduenture ca ſame tyme feſte halowed many greke comynge fro euery coſte temple go pylgrymage theyr vowes acquyte place relyques vyſyte ¶and whan parys dyde eſpye gadred companye worthyeſt cheſe may temple toke right way full well beſene knyghtly wyſe dyde honour ſacryfyce full humbly grekes lyche many ouche iewell ryche golde ſyluer ſtones perre ſpendeth lyke degre quyt hym manly oblacionꝰ deuoutely oryſo • hym demeneth ioye ſe ¶now parys paſſynge great beaute amonges euer alyue none myght wt whym ſtryue troyan greke ſpeke ſemelyhede wonder freſſhe luſty rede porte full lyke gentyll knyght whoſe perſone haue ſyght gan preaſe nyghe fere ryally hym gere coueyte hye eſtate lowe greatly knowe men aſke beſely fro whenſe came cauſe comynge enquerynge one one prudently kepte euerychone thynge openly eſpyde theyr anſwere ſo haue gyde euery thynge kept ſecree eueryche ſo auyſee albe ſome openly declare ne lyſte nat ſpare tolde playnely cauſe comynge pryam ſtronge myghty kynge fader moſte ryall renowne came alſo exyowne thus eche gan rowne pryme face whan came towne therupon ymagynatyfe sore muſynge inquyſityfe eche ſuſpeccion demynge therof lyke theyr oppynyon ratheſt thynge ne knewe folkes done thynges newe whyles mater treate ſondry wyſe amonge theyr wordes greate ſaynge gan anone atteyne eres quene eleyne nygh beſyde region whan ſhe herde reuelacion reporte came bytwene fayre eleyne freſſhe luſty quene anone ſhe ſothe vnderſtode without taryenge abode haſteth hir ſolempnyte freſſhe folke frygye ſe well god wote hir entencion ſe parys deuocion vnder colour holy pylgrymage temple ſhe taketh hir vyage great meyne ryall parayle parys ſe ſhe wyll nat fayle ala luſty new fyre hath hir herte en • lawmed deſyre go vigiles outher ſpectacles none holyneſſe myracles hath meued hir ſhall befall maner woman drawe thether platly conclude ſure multytude gadred lyberte ſe fynde opportunyte theyr deſyre full narowe awayte couertly theyr eyen bayte place ſette theyr pleaſaunce pryuely haue theyr dalyaunce ſome ſygne caſtynge eye token ſhewyng herte drye touche handes ſtole amonge preſe arme fote catche vp theyr leſe lyſt fre bonde nature hym holde honde ayen whoſe ſleyghte auayleth wyt myght lyſte wronge ryght ay acheue ſaythe ye nay agayne whoſe luſt defende hym man may thus guydo aye curſed falſe delyte ſpeke harme hath caught appetite thorughout boke woman ſay yll tranſlate agayne wyll hath aye ioye theyr honour tranſuerſe ſory muſte reherce felle wordes boke founde woman ſo moche bounde • e echone ſo goodly ſo kynde dare nat ſay fynde guydoes wryte thorughout troye boke whan redde fere herte quoke veryly wyttes gan fayle whan therof made reherſayle lyke decrete guydo quyt ye ſhall anone chyt quene eleyne cauſe ſhe went deuoute herte hir offrynge preſente temple venus goddeſſe thus worde worde ſaythe hir expreſſe mortall harme moſt drede fraude • aſte ſleyghte womanhede euery wo gynnynge crop rote agaynſt whiche helpe may bote whan luſt hath dryue theyr herte auayle aye dedely venyme ſeweth tayle whiche man hath power reſtreyne recorde take quene eleyne ho • e brente ala hir deſyres newe luſte dele ſtraungeres ſhe knewe nat ne neuer ſawe aforne thorugh ala full many mē lorne cruell dethe embraced cheyne without pyte ſay thou quene eleyne gooſt ſpiryte ala hath meued sool fro thy lorde ſuche royalte thy hous go amonge preaſe thou wery lyue home peaſe wente ſtraungers ſe takynge hede vnto thyn honeſte thou ſhuldeſt haue kept thy cloſet ſecretly nat haue paſſed ſo folyly abſence thy lorde ala thou wylfull rakell • ſe afore ſhulde ſewe ſoone thou drawen mewe coude nat kepe home thy boundes thou wenteſt hare amonge ye houndes caughte wylfulneſſe thy deſyre coudeſt nat compeſſe though thy luſte lyſt nat refrayne many woman hath caught trayne theyr goynge ſuche halowes ſeke ſyt better ſelfe kepe cloſe theyr chamber fle occaſiowne neuer ſhyp ſhulde peryll drowne ſcatre rocke tempeſtrent carybbes deuoured ſhent go wrake weders ylle kept hauen ſtylle wyll nat occaſions eſchewe drede peryll ſewe muſte amonge neceſſyte ware endure aduerſyte nat hir fote fro trappes ſpare let hir ware ſhe falle ſnare harme done late compleyne whylom worthy quene eleyne hir ſelfe kept home cloſe hir ne ſo wycke loſe reported ye • grene fre ſhe newe whoſe chaūce vnhappy ethe man ought rewe cauſe ſuche deſtruccion • many worthy confuſion hir worthy huſbonde many mo grekes ſyde troye alſo ſtorye ye ſhall rede ſo quene faſte ſhe may ſpede temple hath way nome full ryally whan ſhe come full deuoutly within citheron made vnto venus hir oblacion preſence ſyght many one many iewell many ryche ſtone whan parys eſpyed temple anone hath hym hyed full thryf tely haſte myght whan firſte ſyght goodly fayre freſſhe quene cupides darte whet ſo kene ware hath hym marked ſo aſtoned ne wyſte meruayleth hir great ſemelyneſſe hir womanhede hir porte hir fayreneſſe neuer afore ne wende nature coude haue made ſo fayre creature aungellyke ſhe hir beaute femynyne ſo goodly ſe dempte lyklyneſſe hir beaute ſome goddeſſe herte dyde hym aye aſſure ſhe mortall creature heuenly fayre ſo celeſtyall thought ſhe party conſydereth auyſely hir future ordre ententyfly within reaſon euery thynge good inſpeccion hir golden heer lyke ſonne ſtremes freſſhe phebus wt bryght bemes goodlyhede hir freſſhely face replenyſſhed beaute grace euen ennewed quyckeneſſe colour roſe lylye flour egally nouther wyte thorugh none exceſſe moche lyte within cerclynge hir eyen bryght paradys compaſſed hir ſyght thorugh abreſte beaute wolde perce certaynly ſhall reherce hir ſhap hir fourme future guydo dothe ordre ceryouſly hede fo • e clerely deuyſe haue none englyſſhe therto may ſuffyſe wyll nat tunge nat lyke wante floures alſo rethoryke ſewe flouryſſhyng gay peynture deſcryue ſo fayre creature coloures feble faynte nouther ennewe well paynte eke nat acqueynted • uſe myn therfore excuſe echone nat neclygence defaute oonly eloquence remytte guydo ſe deſcryueth ordre hir beaute take preſumpciowne ¶but wyll tell parys vp downe gothe temple eye caſte towarde eleyne gan preſe faſte brente hoote loues fyre enflawmed greatly deſyre ofte chaungeth countenaunce chere euer neygheth hir nere nere ydarted thorugh hir eyen tweyne agayne warde freſſhe quene eleyne hoote brente herte pryuely albe man outwarde coude eſpy ſhe thought ſhe neuer afore men euer yet bore se none ſo fayre lyke hir pleaſaunce hym loke hir ſuffyſaunce temple ſhe toke hede right nought compaſſe caſte hir thought ſhe may catche opportunyte hym ſpeke good lyberte hooly hir beſyneſſe hym ſhe felte ſo inly great diſtreſſe ofte ſhe chaungeth coūtenaunce hewe venus hath marked newe hir brondes fyred feruence enflawmed ſodayne influence egally brought rage ſaue eye atwe • e meſſage eche ſo fyxe hath caſte theyr ſyght conceyue wyſte • one ryght within themſelf theyr herte mente ne • e hir euer parys wente ſeke fully gete occaſion myght full relacion theyr hertes conceyt declare ſecretly ſo vefell parys nygheth nye place quene eleyne stode hir ſee ther wene tweyne broke ſūme theyr herte gaue yſſue theyr inwarde ſmerte done lyſt eſpyed whan people moſte occupyed temple • ſtare gaſe maſe kepte cloſe worde aſterte man treſon myght aduerte twayne ne wolde mene laſte parys quene concluded haue ſhort auyſement fully fyne theyr bothe entent ſette purpoſe betwyxe certayne whan caſte mete agayne lyſte men hadde ſuſpeccion made ende without ſermon departe albe lothe ſoberly anone parys gothe temple herte euery parte wounded thorugh loues firy darte ſhyppes helde right way anone haſte may whan aſſembled chyualrye one companye fewe wordes ſhortly tofore tale thus gan sy•res quod ſhortly expreſſe cauſe kouthe yor worthyneſſe fader grece v ſente ye knowe chefe entent recure ſuſter exyon handes kynge thelamon whiche thynge ought eſpye impoſſyble ſhortly myn eye waye fer ſe ſo great ſtronge countre allyes aboute euery ſyde herte • ſo inly full pryde yelde hir vp hath nat diſdayne therof treate nat vayne therfore beſte deuyſe syth power may nat ſuffyſe werrey hym regyowne nat egall myght renowne lacke men hym holde felde may nat ſemble ſpere ſhelde encountre hym multytude wherfore beſte conclude ſyth fortune hath v hyder brought goddes haue eke v wrought graciouſly make v londe venus temple faſte ſtronde whiche haboundeth full great rycheſſe grekes offrynge vnto goddeſſe londe ſee fro many ſondry porte men woman haue reſorte place worſhyp venus wyfe kynge menelaus preſent full ryche well beſeyne manhode myght atteyne rauyſſhe hir temple ſpoyle theyr treaſoure cheſen coyle chefe iewelles charge ſomers golde ſyluer take pryſoners maugre ſhyppes brynge ſame nyght without taryenge may nat fayle euer ſay nay ye aſſente ryche pray wherfore haſte ye redy make euery man anone harnes take arme hym well beſte aray• aſſente without delay theyr ſhyppes byde tyll nyght whan phebus chare wt drawen lyght vnder wawes ſterres dyd appere heuen theyr ſtremes clere moone tyme dyde ryſe ſhope forthe full thryfty wyſe manly troyans ſtele armed bryght temple holdynge theyr way ryght caſte lenger tarye proudely entre ſentuarye chapell called citheron without reuerence deuocion done venus hir oratorye clene theyr memorye honour drede obſeruaunce fynally theyr attendaunce myn auctor ſothely diffyne right nought oonly rauyne toke came hande rycheſſe treaſour lande golde ſyluer ſtones iewelles relyques ſacred holy eke veſſelles without abode ſacrarye yfere theyr ſhyppes carye wonder thynke gode kylle ſ • e withſtode pyte ſe blede many grekes ſhyp lede lyued captyuyte full many yere troye cyte ¶and whyles goth parys eleyne hir embraceth armes tweyne full humbly great reuerence fonde maner reſyſtence ſat hir nat ſhe ſo womanly parys ſhe yolde hir vtterly hir herte hap yolde ſhe came therfore yelde hir ſhe hadde leſſe fere nat ſtryue woman ſholde anone gentylleſſe wolde comforteth hir beſte may ladde hir hym without delay ſhyppes full beſyly ſette wardes kepe hir honeſtly whyle retourneth temple agayne ſpoyle robbe make playne thorugh temple walles wyde ¶now ſtode caſtell faſte beſyde yſtuffed well grekyſſhe ſouldeours whiche awoke noyſe pylours ſame nyght gan make ſhoute therwithall anone yſſue oute armed ſtele temple reſkewe manfully ſewe ſo befylle whan togydre mette ſperes ſharpe ſwerdes kene whette ¶they ran togydre tygres vnmylde lyke wodelyons theſe bore wylde faynynge founde fyght albe felde departed aryght troyans doubled noumbre vtterly grekes encoumbre myſchefe made flee purſue cruelly ſlee without mercy caſtell gate reſcuſe came late ſkarmyſſhe fyne deth yolde vp breth myghtely troyans aſſayle withſtande wolde nat auayle manhode felde haue wonne cruelly begonne haſte ſpoyle caſtell ſhyppe brought euerydell treaſour golde may wyn morowe ſayle begyn stuffed good grekyſſhe ſee towarde coſtes troye cytee ſee calme fully theyr wylle bothe tempeſt ſtormes ylle clere alſo bryght heuen ſpace almoſte dayes ſeuen caſtell called tenedowne aryue ſixe myle fro towne glad lyght lande wente fynde parys ſente meſſager ſtreyght vnto kynge hym enfourmeth home comynge theyr expleyt tolde hym euerydele pryamus lyketh wonder wele ſo manly haue borne oute made puplyſſhe towne aboute tydynges great ſolempnyte hye lowe thorugh cyte ioye moſt leſte remembraunce halowe holde feſte thanke theyr goddes full humble wyſe obſeruaunces ſacryfyſe theyr auters great deuocion whyle tenedon holdeth ſoiour quene eleyne whiche gan reufully compleyne hir vnkouthe lyfe dwelle ſtraungers deſolate amonges pryſoners fer ſequeſtred away hir countre solytarye captyuyte wepeth cryeth pytous chere burbly wawes hir eyen clere lyke welle ſtremes hir chekes rayne conſtraynt hir inwarde payne full ofte daye hir ſonge welaway ſobbynge voyce ſhe ſo fer away departed hir menelaus whoſe abſence rage furyous hir lyfe ſhe hateth curſeth eke fortune wo ſhe euer doth contune without ſoiour alway hir bretherne pollux caſtore loue hir doughter dere pale grene ſhe wexyth hir chere whylom freſſher ſene lyllye ſtalke gren • ala chaunged hir roſen hewe euer hir wo encreaſeth newe lyke woman ſhe beholde aye ſhe wepte ſhe water wolde tyll laſte hir heuyneſſe parys hir came gentylleſſe hir comforte appeſe hir rage beſyeth hym hir ſorowes aſwage sayeng hir may mene ye ala goodly freſſhe quene lyſt thus ſelfe ſorowynge diffygure wonder greatly ye may endure moche water cauſeles ſhede wepynge haue dewed ſo wede lyke conduyte ſtremes ran downe lyke penytaunt contryciowne ye diſ • aye ala ſo let fare let ouer go wepynge thought heuyneſſe lady diſtreſſe make ende greuaunce eaſe comforte pleaſaunce men may truſte well ye ſhall haue folye ſorowe thus raue let paſſe ouer theſe ſharpe ſhoures trouthe ye youres lyſt ſhall haue ſuffyſaunce ferforth habundaunce ye hadde amonge grekes enſure thynge fere ſhall holde haue hyght trouthe trewe knyght worde dede herte entere ſhe anone dolefull chere ſhe myght ſobbynge tho ſuffyſe anſwered agayne full lowly wyſe wo • e quod ſhe lothe leſe syth caught take myſchefe vnto wyll may nat ſeye ſo bounde muſt obeye vnder daunger may nat flee holde diſcryued captyuytee ¶ye wot alſo nature drede ne longeth vnto womanhede ſtraunge ſoyle ſtryue rebelle namely hir quarelle shall haue fauoure ſuſteyned lyſt haue pyte myne goodlyhede ye may god deſerue thanke mede wyll rewarde iuſtely tho comforte care wo lady myne quod parys may lyke deuys ſhalbe truſte right wele trouthe fer fele thynge may pleaſaunce ye ſhall haue habundaunce enſure heſte nat fallyble nat agaſte fully credyble wordes heſtes euerychone therwithall ladde hir right anone place royall apparayle comforte hir wolde auayle ſecretly betwene two parys firſte without spake vnto hir ſayde lady dere fayne nat ſpeke herte entere hope ye ſhall dede fynde wherfore pray enprente mynde ſay remembraunce ſaye ſythe ye purueaunce goddes brought thereto fortune eke wyll ſo dare afferme playnly fyrſte diſpoſed haue nat wyrſte good ſo ye muſt take wherfore rede let ouer ſhake heuyneſſe loke ye glad lyght countre though ye owne lande faythfully vnderſtande ye ſhall haue moche habundaunce euery parte full ſuffyſaunce may pleſaunt thynge dare make auaunt countre ſhalbe founde plente paſſe habounde rychely grekes yonder though ye fro ſonder lande called achaye ye haue cauſe ſo diſmaye syth worſhyp reuerence honour gretter excellence ye ſhalbe cheryſſhed ye afore ye playne ye haue forbore owne lorde left ſole ye make wo dole ye ſhall haſte ſette better eaſe certaynely ſo nat diſpleaſe offende vnto womanhede ſtede hym purpoſe drede wedde trewe man loue ſerue euer without feynynge lyues ende lowly kynde dilygent laborous whylom menelaus euery thynge luſtes obeye haue trouthe tyll tyme deye ¶and though wordꝭ playne loue god haue diſdayne requeſt grutche nat leſte ſtocke royall deſcended come hye blode menelay byrthe gode loue trewe euer chaunge newe ¶wherfore ſtynte thus playne wepe let ſome comforte boſome crepe wo appeſe whiche nat worthe hawe ſome myrthe let herte adawe beſeche womanhede wordes take hede ¶alas quod ſhe myght befalle haue left frendes one alle ſtraunge lande alone ſhulde made mone haue cauſe god wote pleye chekes kepe dreye ſalte teres ala wyll nat none ende myn aduerſyte good fayth agaynſt kynde ſodaynely put mynde thylke thynge ioye ſmerte worlde ſytteth next herte ala ſo ſore deſtrayned ſythe goddes haue ordayned better chaunce hope vnto muſt take gre humbly accepte alſo theyr ſonde feble theyr power withſtonde wherfore ſhall agayne wyll ſtryue albe wo herte fele ryue conſente lowly admytte thylke thynge fro whiche may nat flytte maugre wyll neceſſyte fully obeye ye lyſt wyll nat helpe though ſayde nay thus ſhe payneth euer ſhe may lytell lytell hir ſorowe aſwage ſhulde ſhe aye lyue wo rage leſe hir ſelfe ſo tendre creature herte ſtele ne myght nat endure aye woman maner kynde nat ſorowe make ende tyll leyſer haue wept theyr fulle laſte whan gynne dulle make ſorowe happe faſte grace ſoone ouer caſte lyghtly catche comforte theyr ſmerte ſo tendre yt men may conuerte wo ioye thought diſſeuer ſtorme may laſte euer clerkes wyſe bokes lyſt diſcerne thynge vyolente may nat eterne ſtormes phebus bryghter ſo comforte counſayle paris dawed hir olde ſorowe euen lyke glad morowe kynde ſeweth derke blacke nyght proceſſe hir herte wexeth lyght hir wepynge dryed welle lyke ſtorye ſhall anone v tell ¶how parys receyued troye home comynge howe wedded fayre eleyne capytulo xiiij whan quene called eleyne adawed hir drery peyne wawes hir heuy chere hir chekes gonne clere parys herte freſſhe amerous haſte hath ſente kynge pryamus hors men apparayle clothes golde full noble entayle made eleyne wrought none ryche perle many ſondry ſtones agayne hir comynge troye towne parys fro tenedowne shappeth hym lede hir troye pryamus mette weye full ryally faſte may hye many lorde companye full many lady freſſhe well beſeyne many mayde ryde ageyne firſte eſtates comuners hadde parys pryſoners set ordre tweyne tweyne rode next quene eleyne dephebus vpon ſyde knyghtes enuyrondyde ryde next hym rode worthy eneas troyan called pollydamas meyne ſuynge eche degre gentylmanly ioye ſe eeche kepynge certayne ſpace forthe rode ſofte pace tyll kynge mette ſodaynly receyued ſolempnely beſte coude goodly toke reyne hande quene eleyne hir conueyed forthe cyte great preaſe abode ſe ſondry folke ſhoued faſte croude ſhyrle trumpettes yreyſed loude vp ſkye goth blyſfull ſowne whan people entreth towne many nother dyuerſe inſtrument tofore gate went ſondry wyſe made melodye heuenly armonye muſyke touched vpon ſtrynge corde euen one iuſtly accorde wolde herte rauyſſhe ioye whan entred troye amydde palayſe kynge pryamus alyghte anone faſte euer myghte chambre ryche well beſey quene eleyne haſte doth conuey cōmaundynge herte wyll thought offycers hir fayle nought thynge ſhe bethynke ſpyces parted anone ye wyne drynke kynge toke leue tyll ſuppyre ſhe whyles chaungeth hir attyre ¶but ioye towne euery place men went vp downe rude ſothely wryte moche herte troyans delyte ſafe ſounde retourned parys wende haue ioye paradys ſo well ſped iourne hath nat one loſte meyne wherof herte glad lyght haſte next nyght wryte guydo without taryeng longe erely morowe afore large ſonge pallas temple myn auctor ſayth aſſured othe eke fayth bonde wedlocke hym eleyne euer laſte atwene tweyne knotte knyt ſacrament thus done fully aſſent firſte kynge alſo aduyſe cyte fauour paryſe ſo feſte great ſolempnyte contynued moche ryalte weddynge myrthe ſolace thorugh towne eyghte dayes ſpace ſhulde wryte reuell ye daunces freſſhe aray countenaunces ſcole touch lokes amerous pryue grutchyng yt ialous great iuſtes bordes tornaye amydde paleſtre many ſondry playe dyuerſe courſes eke euery feſte large plente done vnto leſte ſtraunge mete maner ſeruyſe haue none englyſſhe deuyſe paſſe ouer nat ¶but whan weddynge came ere caſſandra firſte dyde eſpye thouſande ſythe ala ſhe gan crye pytous wo vntruſſed heeres ſayde thus ſpeynte teeres wretched troye errynge caſe within thy ſelfe ſuffre treſpaſe conſente vnto ſuche folye ſuſteynynge foule auoutrye parys ſhulde take vnto wyue quene eleyne whoſe huſbande lyue wofull troye cruell thy fate beware almoſte late tyme come thou ſhalte deſtroyed many fader ſhall ſone ſe hole morowe ſhalbe ſlayne eue amyddes felde wyll hym ſore greue many wyfe ſore ſhall bewepe ſe huſbande large woundes depe gryde thorugh body pale colde grene ala ſhall ye ſorowe mowe ſuſtene wretched moders ſhall ye endure ſe childerne cruell aduenture afore ſlayne without remedye wyll nat helpe though ye clepe crye moder myn eccuba quene ſhalt thou byde ſharpe ſtoundes kene thy worthy ſones ſeafore ſlawe felde cruelte idrawe blynde people deth thou takeſt hede ne wyl thou worke rede caſe prudent wyſe take away eleyne fro parys right requereth without hir lorde iuſtely hir reſtore ¶what trowe ye thefte cruell dede shall paſſe thus nay nay without drede ſwerde vengeaūce ſhall full ſharpe byte offence ſhall bere wyte paleys hous ſe within throwe toures hye layde erthe lowe ala ala ſaye eleyne vnhappy woman cauſer peyne harde vnſely alſo graceles vnwelfull woman diſtourbler pe thou haſt v brought myſchefe kyndled bronde ſette v afere ala thou arte grounde roote many drery feſte fymerall ſhall beholde amonge v towne wyſe caſſandra vp downe aboute ran ſubarbe ſtrete cryeth euer euer ſhe mete full ofte ſythe ala welaway tyll pryamus bycauſe hir affray noyſe ſhe dyde make without anone doth hir take bynde faſte fetred pryſon without mercy remyſſyon toke hede hir ſadde trouthe hir wordes routhe ſhet hir vp bondes great ſtronge without pyte ſhe abydde longe thus pryſon whyle leue hir morne grekes wyll agayne retourne vnhappy tyme ye ſame whyle fortune falſely gan ſmyle vpon troyans bad merye whiche hyely gan theyr goddes herye wenynge ioye haue aſſured wele thyng aduertynge turnynge ye whele hir laſteth ſtable throwe whā men moſt truſte hir ſhe make amowe tourne hir forhede hir face wrythe suche ioye ſhe hath hir doubylneſſe kythe wrappe hir clereneſſe vnder cloude agaynſt whoſe myght mā may hȳ ſhroude whā ſhe moſt flatereth thā ſhe l • ſt tryſte ioye troyans lytell wyſte ſhe mente theyr confuſiowne whyle aboute towne wende grekes haue goten full recure theyr damage euer haue ſure thorugh thylke praye parys wonne wycked fame rumoure yronne ſwyfte wyngꝭ yt haue wrought menelay tydynges ybrought whyles abode neſtor pyra firſte temple cithera ſpoyled robberye golde treaſoure tyrannye vpon men troyans execute aſſaylynge ſute grekes made cruelly ne ſpared vtterly man woman came theyr waye ne toke ladde praye theyr ſhyppes alſo fyght afore caſtell nyght ¶and alder laſte hereth wyfe loued moche lyfe tenderly god wote thouſande folde aſtoned herte waxed colde ſtone pale hewe hertely wo ſo inly gan renewe firſt whan herde hir name ſowne without anone fell ſwowne ne myght endure ſtande tyll duke neſtor toke hym hande hym awoke deedly ſwowgh ala quod haue loſt howgh lyues luſte hertely ſuffyſaunce come deth make greuaunce fully ende thy cruell darte wounded thorugh euery parte herte alſo korue euery peyne wyfe myn owne eleyne deuorced frome welaway farewell ioye farewell myn olde play haue ſtraungers poſſeſſion whiche wyll full confuſion ala noot cheryſſhe trete fayre eleyne ſo mete ye gone penſyfeneſſe ſlethe may nat wayte dethe • amyd wo menelay ſhope hym go reygne lytell beſyde axeth hors ſayde wolde ryde sool complayne yt felte hym greue whyle neſtor wyll nat leue go hym conſolacion frendely right hauynge compaſſion hym comforte full myght • edynge hym many worthy knyght reygne menelaus firſte • ſtorye telleth v ſente agamenon caſtor come hym anon pollux myght whan come thre ſawe brother ī ſuch myſchef brought almoſte murdred owne thought without abode wyſe agamenon gyue hym comforte conſolacion dyde labour dylygence entere sayenge hym right ye ſhall brother myn wo heuyneſſe deedly ſorowe thus inly may oppreſſe knyghtly herte trouble manhede furyouſly iwys nede though right requered vtterly ſorowe hadde cauſe yet ſemeth iuſte prouydence ye ſhuld ſlyely diſſymule offence syth eche wyſe man aduerſytee shulde fayne chere kepe ſecree inwarde wo bynde hym diſtreſſe manly force ratheſt compeſſe ſpirite ire melancolye people ſooneſt myght eſpye doctryne prudent whan man furye rent fayne chere tyll tyme ſe leyſere vengeaunce kyndele may fyere ſorowe ſhewed ſhall nat fayne ſo taketh hede doth thynges twayne cauſeth frendes ſyghe ſore enemyes reioyſe thy frende herte ſorye nature thyne enemye glad thy myſaduenture wherfore herte whā wo doth moſt haboūde fayne gladneſſe thyne enemye confounde ſhewe chere thou roughteſt nought moſte greuous thy thought wher thou haſt moſt mater complayne make good face glad porte ye fayne teres though thou diſtylle rende thy ſelfe thou woldeſt ſpylle helpeth nat legge thy greuaunce nouther honour purſute vengeaūce ſorowe makynge mowe execute though laſt ay ther cometh therof fruyte men lay diſſymule wronge ſlyghe herte ſtronge peſyble ſmerte token hath manly herte nat wepe woman theyr rage whiche contrary hye courage worde wepyng auēge payne meanes worſhyp attayne let v ſwerde nat wordes fyght tunge appeſe māhod preue myght worde wynde water wepe though tempeſt floddes depe two encreaſe euer moo may nat augment woo ſoon therof whan bothe dole heuy chere encraſe ioye wherfore brother whyle acoye cruell tourment bynde ſo ſore prouerbe hath ſayde full yore proweſſe manly knyght proued moſte myſchefe myght aſſured ceryouſly muſte offencion thorugh neclygence preſumpcion ſette euen amyddes twayne great cauſe haue mater complayne antropoſe vpon hir enuye brake threde made dye noble galfryde poete brytayne amonge euglyſſhe yt made firſt rayne golden dewe droppes rethoryke ſo fyne rude langage oonly enlumyne god praye ſoule haue whoſe helpe nede muſte craue ſeke boke lefte behynde goodly worde therin fynde ſet amonge croked lynes rude whiche wryte ſymylytude rubyeſtant ſo royall renowne within rynge coper latowne ſtant makynge hym douteles amonge bokes englyſſhe pereles eſye knowe ſo excellent makynge equypollent halte ſo taketh hede medle makynge without drede whan wolde ſtyle counterfete may alday colour grynde bete tempre aſour vermylyon holde preſumpcyon foloweth nat therfore lette firſte wyll excuſe procede haue begonne thorugh fauour certayne konne troye boke make ende lefte agayne wyll wende vnto cryſeyde though ſocour rethoryke haue flour hewes ryche ſtones perre bare curyouſte thorugh crafty ſpeche enbroude wt hir ſleue yet wyll nat leue bolde bayarde blynde caſte peryll way fynde right ſo wyll ſtomble forthe hede vnconnynge take better hede hir beaute diſcryue ſothe tho lyue one
