occaſion aye ſtody contemplacion ſondry bokes ſhe wolde hir occupye ſpecyally aſtronomye ¶of prophecye ſpirite ſhe ſome men ſaye ſhe one thre woman cebylebare name y• renowne floureth fame vnto day yet full grene tell yonge polycene diſcryue hir beate vp downe ſothe preſumpciowne take ſo great thynge clymbe ſo hye paſſe connynge sythe nature forgynge mayde hir connynge vtterly aſſayde make hir fayre aboue eche creature ¶and ſayde proudely ſe nature whan lyſt enbellyſſhe werke lyke phebus amonge cloudes derke paſſynge clere ſo comparyſon worke operacion right lyſte adourne make fayre paynte floriſſhe ſhall nat appayre coloures ſo craftely diſpoſe lylye freſſhe roſe ſo ennewe ſhall nat fade aye one wyſe made dere doughter ye knowe mene yonge freſſhe fayre polycene ſkaunce none crafte thus hir worke boſted vtterly nature hir ſelfe whan ſhe may wrought ſhe fully hir herte thought aboue make hir excelle beaute welle ther withall ſhap ſtature ne lacke dare well aſſure god aboue gaue hir ſoueraynte thewes woldeſhe ſhulde crop roote named womanhede fulſomneſſe goodlyhede paſſyngly ydelneſſe preſume expreſſe hir beaute vayne trauayle well wote myn englyſſhe wolde fayle ſuche mater talke felyngely euer certayne nat therfore paſſe ſtreyght wyll go mater dare mo boke maketh menciowne grece troye towne ſpeciall put mo mynde ye haue herde ſaue ye ſhall fynde ſtorye whan cometh therto theyr knyghthode beſte hath laſtynge ſege maner euerydell right anone ſharpe poyntell wyll dreſſe ſtorye entreate werre tell greate tyme nygheth yore breme wynter wt froſtꝭ hore gan aſwage bytter colde whan apollo paſſed holde ſygne call aquarye fyſſhe fer februarye yronne towarde aryete ſeaſon faynte hete hylles hye gan bemes ſmyte makynge ſnowe fayre flake whyte water kyndely relente whiche aboue valey wente neuer flodes ſodayne thowe grene mede gan ouer flowe y•ſe gan ſtoundemele deſtylle downe fro hylle brokes fylle fomy ſtremes wawes ſmale broke bankes dyde auale whan luſty vere yonge grene recomforted ſonne ſhene whiche lytell lytell hewes aye amendeth vp ſpere titan vp aſcendeth whan marche approcheth braūches ouerall gan blowe equynoccyall veer halowed ſeaſon amerous whan grekes proude courageous hole floure cheualrye aſſembled hooly theyr nauye hauen moſte fame athene tyme bare name ygadred aſſent echone towarde troye ſayle gone great nombre y• ſyth worlde began nat remembred maner man togyder one companye mecyfere ſo paſſynge nauye manly men ſo lyſte take hede ſtorye ye ſhall rede make deſcripcyon myne auctor telleth agamenon worthy kyng hondred ſhyppes brought worthy knyghtes ſtuffed ought menelaus lay moſt ye charge hath wt hym brought ſyxty ſhyppes large lande called sperten boece full manly men came fyfty ſhyppes ſtory telleth thus prothenor archelaus lande called sycomenye came ſyxty ſhyppes companye duke hyght achalapus eke full freſſhe deſyrous helymux erle worthy knyght fyfty ſhyppes enarmed fyght hym brought kynge epiſtrophus oonly helpe kynge cedyus thelamon ayax ſome call full renowmed reken hath fyfty ſhyppes brought iournee ſolemyne royall chefe cytee erles duke many worthy knyght eueryche ſtele armed bryght duke tenter amphiacus erle daryon noble theſeus ylke foure full worthy renowne viage came thelamowne olde neſtor cruell herte thought pylon hath fyfty ſhyppes brought kynge daymes yt full worthy eke kynge hyght alſo thoas brought theyr companye hondred ſhyppes knyghtly forto guye thelamon ycalled cylleus armes felle deſpytous hym brought lande ſo ferre sixe thyrty ſhyppes werre amphymacus kynge polybete thyrty ſhyppes brought flete calcedoyne meryon kynge ydinneus hadde theyr ledynge foure ſcore ſhyppes crete vlixes grekes dyde mete fyfty ſhyppes ſtuffed trace towardes troye proudely pace ¶duke melleus full manly men brought eke hym grete ſhyppes ten moreouer duke perhotacus duke named protheſylaus hauen called athene brought fyfty ſhyppꝭ enarmed bryght ſhene phylyarcha ſtronge myghty yle methaon guydo dothe compyle brother polydris alſo theyr countre trycionyco brought two twenty ſhyppes fynde phyces made mynde achilles came fyfty full nombre rodon troyans encombre came twenty ſhyppes wt kynge thelapolus duke hyght antipus lande heſyda men call whiche folke nyghe cherles ſayle croſſed agayne bryghte heuen nombre came ſhyppes eke elleuen name full famous worthy duke called amphymacus polybethes ſtronge myghty kynge fyfty ſhyppes brought cōmynge richa noble regyowne kynge full worthy renowne loſius duke eke rede fynde noble dyomede ſhyppes great ſpeke ſmall barge hath wt hym brought fro calydonye arge foure ſcore nombre ſothly tale thelemus myghty euryale two manly men armes lage dyomede came vyage polyphebus brought ſhyppes ſeuen phyneus hardy kynge enleuen prothoylus ſpecyfye brought fyfty ſhyppes vnto nauye fro demeneſa myghty regyon carpenor made mencyon brought fyfty eke capadye countre great prouynce whiche kynge trearyus beyſa lorde kynge brought two twenty alſo cōmynge fynally ſhall nat lye full many ſhyppe nauye mo guydo maketh reherſayle towarde troye grekes ſayle omer deſcripcion grekes ſhyppes maketh mencion shortly affermynge y• man neuer borne ſuche nombre ſhyppes ſawe toforne counted ſhyppes palamydes brought hym theyr nombre encreſe whan theſe lordes aforeſayd euerychone kynges duke erles one aſſembled without wene afore hauen called athene famous kynge great agamenown wyſe ſo worthy ſo hye renown prynce gouernoure grekes hooſt anone dyde laboure beſy cure waker dylygence hye aduyſe inwarde prouydence delyuer wyſely nede procede matere caſtynge vp downe reuoluynge hye diſcreciowne may ſo begyn ende conclude well wylfulneſſe ne ſhende hooly theyr purpoſe thorugh rakelneſſe ne thorugh none haſte without auyſeneſſe may afore ſo wyſely ſe fynally felycyte may accōpliſſhe purpoſe ī certayne ſo kynge vpon large playne cyte lytell fro ſtronde lordes wyll thynge wonde haue counſayle wyſe agamenon makynge anone conuocacyon ſuche moſte great inſpecyall ſyttynge firſte ſee royall lordes eueryche ſee lyke hye lowe degree tumulte ſtynted ſcylence thorugh y• prees gyue hym audyence anone full ſobre wyſe began tale ſhall deuyſe syres quod praye take hede ſo noble ſo renowmede wyſdome worthyneſſe manhode eke hye proweſſe knyghthode reporte fame thorugh y• world reboūdeth yo • name douteles floure chyualrye men may fynde companye whoſawe euer manly men yfere togyder met yonge ſo freſſhe ſo couragyous alſo well beſene haue orſo lykely ſythe worlde began without raſkayle ſo many knyghtly man kynges duke many another lorde wyll one accorde one herte aſſembled place fortune goddes theyr grace nat behynde iourney repreue may nat fayle purpoſe acheue ¶for deme hym playnely arage wer • e wood durſte vyage wyſe perturbe preſume take agayne v outher aſſume myght hym malys excyte worthyneſſe neuer ſo lyte v prouoke ire offence ne ſhulde mortall recompence aquyte mede lyeth myght haue amōge v ſo many worthy knyght amonges whiche hondred yet mo coude cheſe able go manly force knyghtly ſuffyſaunce take hym vengaunce vpon troyans hymſelfe alone whiche gadred echone men ſuffycyent execute ſūme entent accomplyſſhe felycyte cauſe mene whiche aſſembled bothe hye lowe nat vnknowe ſhamefully troyans haue v greued prouoked v wylfully ymeued ryſe agayne haue recure ryght wronges done force myght wherfore let v one aſſente wyll sette haue right ſkyll redreſſe fynde complayne one herte beſy payne vpon troyans werre make ſuppoſe ſhall ſo awake ſhall lerne thenſe wende remembre worldes ende hereafter ſhall dare take hande preſume grece lande bolde whyle haue lyfe ſpace agayne grekes treſpace whoſe offence ſayth late within herte ſo brennynge hate feruent hete gredy yre fro day day ſo ſetteth v fyre reneweth conſtreynt payne inwardely ſhall nat fayne muſt reaſon ſo hye greuaunce ſelfe enforce vengaunce right requereth iuſte ſorowe compelleth v bothe eue morowe troyans harmes bewreke ſtoppe tunges ſo ſpeke reprefe vylenye muſt attones ſhape remedye foon henſforthe may drede worſe v god forbede tyme cōmynge thorugh pacyence lykely ſuffre theyr importable offence paſſe forthe take nohede syth neuer yet grekes coude rede man dyde reprefe theyr name iuſtely myght rebounde theyr ſhame withouten quyte agayne thorugh theyr manhode ſo openly playne man myght ſeyne wyſe reporte amys new ſhall nat diſſymule caſe chere oppreſſed dredefull face let ſlyde lyghtly ouer go great offence ſo late whiche wolde tourne vnto v oures great reprefe ſucceſſoures tyme cōmynge ſhamefully beſpoke grekes vurſte wroke vpon theyr foon whiche may nat enſure ſythe one wyll refourme wronge therwithall ſo myghty ſo ſtronge coude brede lengthe right reherſe power ſtrenthe durſte euer worthyneſſe aſſayle ne ſhulde without fayle repente herte ende rewe saue troyans day newe wylfulneſſe foly rage lande made vyage vnware v theyr pray home wente whiche ſhall full haſtely repente theyr treſpas great offencyowne ¶for worlde knoweth vp downe late gone grekes fewe vpon troyans theyr power dyde ſhewe ſlewe theyr kynge called lamedowne fader pryam kynge towne fordyde toures cyte ſlewe vp comynalte grekes ſwerde yt lyſt ſpare amonge v ſeruytude care cōplayne theyr harme yt may nat recured may ſtande full aſſured agayne v holde chaumpartye haue ſo worthy companye lykely thouſande acheue foure fyue ſo lyghtly myght preue yet one thynge afferme well dare cōmynge troyans well ware theyr laboure theyr dilygence agaynſt v make reſyſtence theyr myght knowe doute gadre frendes countres aboute helpe theym ſtrength theyrnede v withſtande myght ſpede fynally one thynge counſayle hauen ferther ſayle may fortunat one aſſent make ambaſſyat prudently wende delos haſte ſende whiche ile lytell beſyde diſcretely iourney prouyde may haue better hap grace appollo patron place haue hym may ſpede fynall anſwere great nede expleyt ſhall fall ſo ye wyll aſſent counſayle moſt eke leſte echone thought beſte condeſcende concluſyon without contradiccyon attones without drede prayſe counſayle wyſe rede therupon diſcretely oughte ſayth ſtory euen thus wroughte ¶how grekes ſente achylles pyrro de yle delos haue anſwere god appollo ſhulde ſpede iourney capitulo xvij tyme agamenon concluded hath fully reaſon ye haue herde ſentence fyned grekes herte ful enclyned one voyce accorded playnely thus achylles alſo pirrodus comyn profyte ſythe ſage shall take charge meſſage appollo anſwere gone ſhyppe haſte anone ſayle forthe large ſee towarde deluos proſperytee aryued ycome lande whiche yle vnderſtande myn auctor ſayth without le hath ſyght amonges cyclades men rockes haue ſo moche ado amyd ſec called heleſpontico whiche yle make deſcripcyon muſte whyle make diſgreſſyon fro mater myn auctor doth yle iſydorus ſoth reherſeth playnly latona quene appollo firſte dyane ſhene childed hath iubyter hir lorde whan iuno diſcorde wryte ouyde alytell whyle ſo befylle lytell yle temple whylom dedycate vnto appollo alſo conſecrate worſhyp olde foundacyon honoured great deuocyon bycauſe appollo bemes clere flood firſte dyde appere ſhewed horne rather ſoone dyane eke called moone whiche ſhewynge yle bereth name day ſo great fame oonly apperynge ylke twayne delos greke ſayne ſhewynge apparence thus began great reuerence appollo firſte honour eke hym idone ſo many greke ſuſter called dyane pale moone ſo waxe wane called paynems goddeſſe whylom wod huntereſſe lady ſonne hir brother yle hath lordſhyp none oonly theyr natyuyte shewed theyr lyght firſte countre whiche yle grekes alſo calle ortygya theyr langage alle bycauſe curlewes firſte iſeyne otygyas ſeyne curlewe grewe vnderſtande firſte engendred lande ¶and appollo called eke titan tyme ſo moche worſhyp wan longe afore made ſterre iubyter whan helde werre alſo ycalled phebus ſome ynamed phycius pheton victorye whan hym ſtewe encreaſe glorye great ſerpent erthe lowe arowes myghty bowe whiche conqueſte great god cupyde hadde enuye euen thorugh ſyde wounded hym depe herte y• arowe gold yt made hym ſore ſmerte pheton phebus made fyne came phetonyſſes ſo deuyne mene woman deuynereſſes thorugh dede men theſe falſe ſorcereſſes one whylom reyſed samuel loue saule byble tell temple large longe olde ſtature pured golde full great hye huge weyghte therin thorugh deuylles ſleyghte ſpirite vnclene falſe illuſyon gaue anſwere euery queſtyon nat ydoll dombe ſtocke ſtone thus people deceyued euerychone fende brought great errour worſhyppe ſuche falſe honour ſacryfyce curſed mawmentrye wyſe began ydolatrye place telle caſte longe abode laſte compendyouſly purpoſe deſcryue gynnynge ende ye ſhall blyue without ambygnyte byrthe natyuyte criſte iheſu incarnacy owne ydolles braſte fell downe vanyſſhed brought nought whan herodes bleſfull childe ſought thorugh malys cruelte horryble holy wrytte recordeth byble whiche purſuyte perſecucion dyde apere auyſion hooly aungell ioſeph ſlepe bad hym ryſe alſo take kepe vnto childe alſo marye go waye herode hym aſpye egipt great regyon lyke goſpell maketh mencyon right anone came lande none ydoll yt vpright myght ſtāde ſhyuered vnto peces ſmale holy wrytte playnely tale recorded friſte iſaye lorde eſy ſkaye aſcende ſhulde holde forthe weye towarde egipt therwith ſhulde deye mawmetrye longer dwelle iewes recorde yſmaelle firſte mawmetrye fonde made claye ydoll honde paynems wryte telle v alder firſte promotheus founde ydolles ſhortly conclude ſymulacrum cometh ſymylitude thynge playnely lykneſſe made man ymage expreſſe vnto whiche paynems theyr gyſe falſe honour curſed ſacryfyſe begonne firſte ryte drede man ſome ſaye belus firſte began suche falſe worſhyp ſuche mawmettye theyr bokes clerkes ſpecefye aſſirye lorde gouernour whoſe deth ſone honour nynus hyghte ymage dyde make worſhypped oonly ſake brent golde falſe affeccion ſette vp conſolacion mynde memoryall vnto whiche herte wyll ignoraunce fleſſhely loue dyde honour god aboue temple moſte excellence made people reuerence ſayde heuen deyfyed man durſte denyed tyll ſoone lytell whyle wycked ſpyryte folkes begyle ydoll entrede abyde gaue anſwere vpon euery ſyde people lyſte demaunde agayne wyll cōmaunde obeye fully folke aſſyrye whiche vnto god dyde great iniurye makynge people ſuche errour falle ſome belus ſome bell hym calle ſome balym ſome belphegore felle errour alway belzebub named alſo whiche name made wordes two bel zebub thus ſignefye bel god zebub flye belzebub togydre ſpecyfyes ioyned one great god flyes fayned falſe ydolatrye gan worlde worſhyp mawmetrye ¶for ſome saturne god goddes gan theyr errour falſely call whylom myghtykyng crete gaue hym name planete heuen hath ſo large ſpere poetes theyr fable lere thorugh ſapyence sawe dyuyne prouydence ſone ſhulde hym deſcende ¶and iuno goddes wende ſhulde hȳ playnely fro reigne expelle ſuffre hym lenger dwelle kyngdome whan came age wherof saturne fyll ſuche arage wyll ſhape remedye therfore byddynge wyfe whan y• childe bore ſhe hym ſhulde brynge anone ſtede wherof hym ſhe brought ſtone ſaue hir childe ſhe dyde hir beſyneſſe saturne thorugh gredyneſſe ſtone deuoureth melancolye thus saturne bokes lye hadde ſones thre doughter mo iubyter neptunus pluto iubyter gretteſt name moſte renowmed worthyeſt fame amonge paynems veryfyed ſo hye haue hym magnefyed hym calle god fyre eyre nert saturne borne heyre nert hym bokes rede god batayle myghty mar rede next appollo ſo clere ſo ſhene bryght dayes eye voyder nyght cheryſſher fruyte herbe floure corne whiche god lyke ſayde toforne delos worſhypped honoured venus often hath ſocoured many louer fayre luſty quene aledge theyr woundes grene firſte hurte hir firy bronde ſhe goddeſſe many londe worlde hath hir demeyne faſte enbraced hir firy cheyne mene lady called venus next ordre mercurius ſpeche hath moſte excellence rethoryke ſugred eloquence muſyke ſonge armonye hath lordſhyp hole regalye next moone wexe wane called lucyna alſo eke dyane delos hath hir mancyon lyke tofore maked mencyon full myght horned pale ſhe lady chaunge mutabylyte ſelde one halte hir tyme ſo fare borne hir clyme aye delyte thynges newe whoſe herte cladde many ſondry hewe dyuers theyr affeccyons wyſe ſondry regyons mawmetrye venym ronne lyke clerkes well deuyſe konne fynde maurycyens worſhyp iulam egipcyens honoure y• ſis theyr konnynge whylom doughter ynachus kynge taughte thē firſt theyr lōde ere ſowe alſo letter rede knowe lecture ſette theyr beſyneſſe whiche thynge calle hir goddeſſe iubyter honoured crete whylom helde ſouerayne ſete leyde many dyuerſe charge egles beten baner large lorde eyre londe ſee royall kyngdome deuydynge thre hyeſt hymſelfe doth contune hole ſee gaue vnto neptune laſte erthe holde ſee royall gaue pluto god infernall alder laſte whan ſtellyfyed iubyter moſte magnyfyed crete aboute ouer made memoryall large tombe ſtatue lofte hym honoured theyr rytes ofte encens ſacryfyſe mater ferther deuyſe larynes beſy dylygence theyr rytes dyde reuerence goddes credyble y• called fawny muyſyble haue hered wellynge wodes grene albe men theyr fygure may nat ſene romayns deuyne moſte ī honour haue theyr god quyryne whiche whylom bokes telle v amonges called romulus bylte firſte walles towne herde came ſuche renowne thorugh manhode worthyneſſe ſpere bokes ſayne expreſſe hede pytched grounde gan anone lyke founde floryſſhe floure budde myracle nature hadde none obſtacle wexe grene freſſhe blomes newe manhode men hym knewe knyghthode great fame ¶the worthy knyghtꝭ romebare ye name hym quyryte called hye heuen whan ſtalled amonge goddes ydeyfyed thus romeyns haue hym glorifyed theyr god golde great expenſes rede athenyenſes hole herte choſen ſerue goddeſſe called mynerue pallas eke hir criſtall ſhelde neptunus euen amyd felde helde champartye woman theyr ſyde men full ſurquedous pryde defendeth hym gyuynge name athene cyte moſte fame ſayne whether ſhe shulde right name cyte tyll befell gan ſtryue sodeynly ſprange fayre olyue pallas part grene fayre bloſſomynge agayne welle gan ſprynge hym pluto water large depe whiche thynge appollo toke good kepe whiche dome nat reckeles olyue tokeneth loue pe water trouble contek werre ſtry fe gaue ſentence anone diffynytyfe pallas ſhulde called mynerue palme playnely ſtryue diſcerue ſhe anone gaue name towne called hye diſcrecyowne athene whiche ſpeeyall ſayne cyte inmortall wyldome firſte began floure ſkyll cyte dyde honoure myghty pallas goddeſſe ſcyence hir aye moſte hadde reuerence paue theyr regyon whorſhyp moſte quene cytheron mene venus full doubylneſſe afore ſomwhat dyde expreſſe hir temple full ſolempnely ſette hir hyeſt moſte rychely gold aſure hir ſtatue paynte coloures may neuer faynte ſette hir vp hyeſt ſee temple men may ſe ſhe ſtant naked wawy ſee aboute hir goddeſſes thre aſſigned beſy attendaunce awayte hir hir obſeruaunce floures freſſhe blewe rede whyte hir aboute delyte hir hede ſhe hath chapelet roſes rede full pleaſauntly yſet hede downe vnto hir fote ſondry gōmes oyntemerꝭ ſore ennoynte ſwetter ſmelle enuyron poetes telle dowues whyte flyenge eke ſparowes beſyde cupyde arowes hir blynde ſone hurte dere loſeth ofte ſmyte wote nat muſt nedes bycauſe blynde thus honoured moſt mynde amonge people venus goddeſſe naxyens theyr beſyneſſe ſerue bachus myghty god wyne whoſe lycour moſte precyous fyne recomforte hertes glade refreſſhe hewes fade face pale maketh wyttes ſharpe loſeth tunges make loude carpe cauſeth walke lyberte diſcure thynge ſecree without aduyſe diſcrecyon wyne hath domynacyon ſecretneſſe may kept mewe ſome bachus ſerue ſewe amonge hym haue ſuche deuocion ſome whyle voyde reaſon haſty wood without drede ſome alſo ſo toty theyr hede voyde power myght haue foot ſtande vp ryght yet iargaunt pye pale chered glaſy eye full reaſon tyll wynde ſpent man woman vyolent veryly beeſt vnreſonable dome holde eke vnable accepted companye whan theyr tunge wadeth lye ne may brynge forthe worde thus bachus ſtronge myghty lorde ofte cauſeth folkes erre debate make werre haſtyneſſe nede wherfore wyſdome men drede ſleyghty werkynge falle y• ſnare feble braynes meſure ſpare vnwarely areſted take bachus make ſhake feuer worſe tercyen cuſtome cotydyen alterat bachus myghty iou affered tournynge hous fordreynt drye lande whan hath loſte bothe foot hande ſtrawe playeth lyke ape deuoutely gynneth gape • oddeth ofte iowſy hede hadde heuy cappe lede condycyon entre maye relygyon myghty bachus habylyte whiche lorde hath ſoueraynte hony mylke therto bawme ſo ryche alſo lordſhyp hath hye power deuyne bothe grape euery vyne gyue nouryſſhynge influence honour reuerence reyſed moſte vnderſtande amonge vynters euery maner lande bycauſe ſo gracyous lymme worſhyp vulcanus god fyre iubyters smythe whiche forgeth blacke ſlythe great thonder hydous horryble leuenes whylom vyſyble weſt oryent gaſteth v dredefull dent ſmotry ſmythe ſwarte vulcanus whylom herte ſo ialous towarde venus wedded wyfe wherof roſe dedely mortall ſtryfe whan mar gan hir firſte eſpye hye malys cruell falſe enuye thorugh y• ſhynȳge phebus bemes bryght lyenge bedde mar hir owne knyght whiche herte brente glede makynge ſclaundre brode ſprede gan theron falſely muſe god forbede man accuſe • lytell woman euer loue lette harde diſſeuer though ſuche thynge gentylleſſe paſſe ouer lyghtly bere none heuyneſſe leſt thou woman odyous yet ſmythe falſe vulcanus hadde thus eſpyed amonge paynems yet deyfyed ſo falſely woke haue hym ſette laſte boke amonge goddeſſe falſe mawmetrye wyſe gan ydolatrye ye haue herde thorugh oppynyons people errynge theyr affeccyons falſe trouthe cerche techynge holy chirche holy doctryne tradycyons ſhall deſpyſe ſuche oppyons whiche fende founde nat oflate whan aungelles heuen create hadde prelacye prophete called yſaye wryteth right thus cedres grene paradyſe nat ſo fayre ſene planys fyr heyghte ſothe ſayne hyghneſſe myght nat attayne tree ſo delycyous paradyſe natſo precyous nouther ſyght ſemelyneſſe egall hym fayreneſſe thorugh pryde ſurquydrye whan ſayde god ſytte ſo hys wyll lyke alſo ſet ſee hye northe paſſynge degree caſte downe relygyons fayre heuenly manſyons ſodaynely pytte helle perpetuelly dwelle ſayde whan fylle ſo ferre fylle thou ſo thou morowe ſterre myddes ſtones bryght ſo perſynge firy theyr lyght whylom thy great bryghtneſſe called lucyfer criſte ſayth expreſſe goſpell ſawe fro heuene sathan deſcende lyke firy leuene olde ſerpent ſolowe falle heebre • theyr tunge calle ¶bemoth doth latyn playne expreſſe beeſt rude full curſedneſſe vyle ſerpent leuyathan iſydre well deſcryue whiche kynde neuer conuerſaunte welles trouble hath moſte haunte amonges watres large ſee ſayth dauyd lyke ye may ſe sauter makynge mencyon ſnake monſtruous dragon full venym harde grace whiche ſee large great ſpace foule adder hath manſyon vnto mankynde illuſyon whylom ſawe ye holy monke brādan ſayled occyan thorowe de • ecte apytte horryble foule hydous credyble abyde tortuous ſerpent vnto daye playnely iugement malys enuyed ſo mankynde whiche wt gynne ſleyghtes fynde came faders firſte paradyſe deceyue bet deuyſe couertly worme paſſage toke ſerpent lykneſſe ymage chere loke countenaunce lyke mayde hath reſemblaunce woman recordeth bede deceytes rather ſpede mene oonly nat elles behynde ſo clerkes telles lyke ſerpent wombe backe tayle whan gan hym aſſayle towarde eue whan gan glyde firſte enquereth hir roke lyde god forbade eten tree whiche ete ſothly ſhulde lyke goddes knowynge good yll right forthwith gan ſulfyll fendes heſte theyr eyen vncloſed theyr gylte ſodaynely depoſed paradyſe wretchydneſſe lyue laboure ſorowe diſtreſſe thus fende firſte whan hetoke forme ſnake woman loke made tunge hir hede meue falſe engyne mankynde greue doth trauayled wycked ſpirites vaxed aſſayled meue tunges falſely breke blaſphemye thynge y• ſpeke ſame ſerpent leuyathan contunynge aye falſely gan curſed yools dombe▪ v • fe▪ blynde full ofte ſpeketh ſpirites fynde whiche fendes dauid wryte certayne goddes folkes ſo vayne honour rytes ſuperſticious whylom appollo delphicus lyke tofore ye haue herde deuyſe whiche ought inough ſuffyſe trowe cauſe myn auctor reherſeth grounde gynnynge idolatrye cauſe ought eſpye ſawe mater nat knowe lyche well bothe hye lowe perauenture pleſaunce hath grounde put remembraunce falſe goddes mawmetrye moſte poyſye y• ſtorye reſorteth ſoone agayne achilles ye haue herde ſaye pirrodus haue waye ynome temple thyder ycome haue anſwere theyr embaſſatrye great appollo whiche may nat lye preſtes haue theyr counſayle take temple praye wake tyll may fynde vnto theyr entent haue anſwere houre conuenyent theyr purpoſe leyſer opportune ¶and one herte ſo longe contune prayenge faſtynge oblacyons ſacrifyſe ſondry oryſons tofore god awaytynge alway faſte tyll anſwered laſte 〈◊〉 voyce ſayde achilles twye home grekes faſte thou hye thou hyder ſente ſay ſothely ſūme theyr entent shalbe fulfylled without wordes mo ſhall troye go abyde many ſtronge batayle laſte without fayle ten yere daye wynne ſhall towne brynge playnely deſtrucciowne walle toures ſhall falle ruyne theyr purpoſe fyne kynge pryamus ecuba wyfe theyr ſones mortall ſtryfe shall ſlayne brother brother fyne may none ſhall none eſcape place ſuche grekes lyketh vnto grace routhe mercy take ſome thus ende make whiche anſwere achilles glad lyght herte myght thanketh appollo bleſfull eure ſodaynely ſort aduenture ſelfe tyme befyll wonder thynge troye fro pryamus kynge ſent byſſhop ſame ca haue anſwere whoſe name calcas came ſool without pres ſame houre whyle achilles preſent man great ſcyence mene calcas hadde experyence specyally calculacion ſort alſo dyuynacion lerned aſtronomye whan tyme dyde eſpye haue anſwere moſt conuenyent appollo lyke entent tofore maked memorye entred oratorye doynge rytes obſeruaunces lyke cuſtome circumſtaunces beſely gan knele praye thynges deuoutely ſaye god crye calle ful ſtronge appollo wolde nat prolonge sodaynely anſwere gan attame ¶and ſayde calcas twyes name right well ware thou ne tourne agayne troye towne vayne fynally lerne ſhorte tyme ſhall deſtroyed ſothe whiche may nat denyed wherfore wyll thou allyed grekes achilles go anone wyll beſo ſhall haue haue diſpoſed victorye honour may diſpoſed fatall ne may nat varye thou ſhalt neceſſarye counſeylynge yeuynge rede right helpynge theyr good ſpede worde roſe hym vp calcas achilles went eaſy pa whan came preſence great honour moche reuerence receyued lyke eſtate ſoone confederate swore togydre bonde aſſuraunce one without varyaunce haſte togydre gone theyr ſhyppes ſhope forth anone pirrodus goynge theyr ſyde hale vp anker lenger byde ſayle forthe calcas twayne towarde grece nedeth nat complayne wynde wawe tyll aryued athene ſtode vpon ſee large cyte olde foundacion achilles kynge agamenon hath calcas brought alſo pirrodus whan grekes ſtory telleth v aſſembled togyder went tofore kynge calcas repreſent lordes lenger dwell right anone achilles gan tell without abode delos mette tofore appollo anſwere fette god hath playnely determyned grekes purpoſe ſhalbe fyned vpon troyans bad calcas alſo wyſe troye go grekes abyde ſtylle tyll theyr purpoſe fynally fulfylle whiche thynge grekes glad chere calcas accepte herte full entere one confederat bonde one water londe without chaunge varyaunce othe made put remembraunce agayne fully hym aſſure cheryſſhe hym whyle theyr lyfe may dure wele wo ſo made ende parte theyr lodgynge wende tȳll morowe y• ſterry nyght whan aurora gladded wt ye lyght phebus vemes grekes vp aryſe theyr goddes many ſacryfyſe honour maye deuoutly holdynge feſte daye theyr rytes meynt loue drede remembraunce good ſpede anſwere yt goddes haue ſent agreable vnto theyr entent pirrodus achilles amonges pres calcas come tofore agamenon lordes ſyttynge enuyron lyke theyr eſtates eche place dewe humbly gan ſalewe vpon knee ſobre coūtenaunce prayed diſpleſaunce ſtynte whyle gyue hym audyence right anone made ſylence amonge calcas gan abrayde euen thus full ſoberly ſayde osyres quod lordes dere kynges prynces duke sonoble echone worthy famous eke ſo manly ſo vertuous whiche place preſent nat fyne chefe entent cauſe alſo ye echone aſſembled troye togone power great ſtrengthe purpoſe longe drawe lengthe differred forthe fro day daye damage platly naye longe ye ſoiourne yle trowe ye nat pryam whyle hath eſpyes amonge pryuelye wote wele ſaye faythfullye knowe fyne gouernaunce whyles may make purueaunce hym defende whyle ye ydell reſte ſemeth ſothly ye nat beſte abydynge ſuche delayes great harme may fall certayne nay preue thus playnely whyle ye enmyes graunte lyberte puruey may myghty hāde enforce power withſtande theyr frendes theyr allyaunce leyſer make theyr ordynaunce folye ye ſo differre syth ye redy make werre ennemyes euery circūſtaunce thynge may quarell ſo auaunce haſty ſuyte wyll ſharper byte iren hoote tyme ſmyte nat abyde tyll colde nouther plye wyll folde go ſette vpon one accorde ſhyppe anone within borde enhaſte tyme remewe myght quarell purſewe agaynſt haue treſpaſſed many dayes ſomer paſſed many monthes ronne ouer ſlyde titan ofte chare hath ryde eeſt weſt wawes depe ſtremes bathed whyle ye haue leyne aſlepe ſpent tyme place thus whyle wynde called zephyrus benyngnely enſpyred hath lofte tempre eyer wether fayre ſofte calme ſee wawes ſtylle playne whyles ye waſte dayes vayne whan foon therto take hede wyll ſuppoſe drede bolde ſette lyte truſte forſothe wyll quyte trewely lyke bounde thynke ye haue goddes founde towarde benyngne fortunat honour ſaued hye lowe eſtat ſo ſhall forthe ingratytude prouoke nat purpoſe delude wylfully ſlouthe fortune wonder though nat contune towardes ſhewe theyr grace wherfore rede henſe pace demynge grekes playnely ſee weryed faynted hadde longe ſaylynge parbraked forbroke wherfore caue haue wroke ſodaynely ſette hede put themſelfe aduenture drede rakelneſſe vn aduyſely wherof ſelfe vnhappely befell whan grekes mette ſperes longe ſwerdes ſharpe whette eche manhode ſhewe cauſe troyans fewe yſſue dyde folylye felde nat parted egallye grekes innumerable mete troyans nat able tyme myght nat ſuffyſe toke paſſynge hye empryſe yet ne wold thyng thē wdrawe tyll wounded yſlawe ouerlayne grekes vtterly bore downe cruelly mercyles guy dath reporte behoueth home agayne reſorte nede neceſſytee attones gan flee mene ſuche lefte lyue caſtell haſ • ed full blyue ne myght lenger holde felde agaynſt grekes ſpere ſhelde feble ſhortly conclude abyde ſo great multytude flee grekes great paſe ne ceaſe nat ſewe chaſe full haſtely caſtell gate entre cruell fate kyll ſlee hye lowe ſpare none ne lyſte wyghte knowe none eſtate felly hym oppreſſe fonde golde eke rycheſſe vnto ſhyppe caryed anone caſtell lefte nat ſtone aboue another turned vp ſo downe walle toure chefe donge owne thynge ſtode ſo vnder myne whan brought vnto ruyne grekes anone theyr ſhyppes haſte one aſſent purpoſe faſte without abode one wyll herte fro hauen playnely dyuerte ſayle towarde tenedowne ſtronge caſtell whiche fro troye towne diſtaunce ſixe myle ſtode full treſoure rycheſſe gode replenyſſhed habundaunce whan theyr ordynaunce yſayled haue bothe ſafe ſounde fro ſee taken haue grounde theyr pleaſaunce wonder agreable ſyght place delytable holſome eyre ſoyle right fayre grene luſty playnes goodly ſene alſo habundaunt vytayle replenyſſhed may auayle oſteynge ſowgyoures firſte lande full freſſhe floures plenteuous bothe corne grayne wyne fruyt thyng lay barayne beſte foules paſſyngly plente faſte ſtode alſo ſee full habundaunt fyſſhe fynde ſeaſon euery maner kynde whan within caſtell grekesſe londed fere without abode arme went oute vpon make hydous ſhoute stuffyng caſtell wt meyne ſtrong behynde toke theyr way guydo fynde towarde theyr foon knyghtly ſet vpon right forthe grekes eke anon mette vpon ſyde full ſurquydous right full pryde clenly armed harneys ofſtele freſſhe arayed beſene ſo wele felde thycke ſworme eche ſyde men may beholde ſeen spradde playne downe vnto y• ſtronde tyll laſte mette honde honde aſſemble ſquare ſperes grounde hurtle yfere many blody wounde good day ſaluynge ſtrokes felle men herde rynge baſſenettes ſtrokes rounde aboute cruelly fyre ſprange oute amonge tuftes brode bryght ſhene foyle golde fethers whyte grene eke breſtes perced many ſhelde beſagues fleed brode felde many men ley mortall founde full dedely pale lawe grunde face gruf blody ſtremes wyde aldermoſt vpon grekes ſyde ſlaughter diſcomfyture myghtely troyans dyde endure tyll laſte ſo ſewe multytude grekꝭ thē hewe mo forty agaynſt one force abacke muſte gone thyng lacke manhode dare ſayne ſo many haue ouer layne may lenger felde ſoiourne theyr caſtell home agayne retourne full great haſte ſuche myght eſcape away lyue ſome rape drede deth toke flyght horſe backe troye towne full ryght wonder though haſte faſte gate chace grekes laſte cruelly purſewe ſome myght nat remewe troye ſyde forweryed fyght grekes ſlewe theyr full myght myght attayne may raunſome mercy gayne none eſtate without excepcyowne vnto tenedowne grekes went ſette aboute troyan none myght eſcape whan hadde bulwerkes wonne ſkale walle begonne made ſaute manfully ofte troyans ſtode lofte put entre ne myght caſte ſtone quarell bryght bowe turkey ſhote arbalaſteres theyr gonners ſtandynge corneres hym alſo caſte wylde fyre yrous hate full hote theyr deſyre lyke manly men ſelfe diffende aye grekes vp aſcende cruelly put grounde tyll without ordynaūce haue founde gynne deuyſed none gonne great caſte ſtones bent toures right lyne large ſowes lowe myne ſome vpon walle gone ſo thycke made lyme ſtone entre many wayes ſeke sette theyr baſtyles theyr hurdeys eke rounde aboute harde walle ſkalynge ladder ſaw • e marcyalle gan vp caſte hokes holde vp aſcende ſturdye grekes bolde tyll troyans creſtes caſte great ſtones whyle wolde laſte callyowne eke grekes opreſſe wonder manly dyde theyr beſyneſſe theyr diffence made plonge lowe caſte quarell ſhote bowe thorugh olyettes neceſſyte put may none broke theyr neckes theyr ſhuldre boues felle ſquare ſtones lye dede pyteous pale hewe grekes aye gan ſaute renewe multytude troyans aſſayle withſtande gan fayle wexe feble reſcuſe came none ſo force grekes gone thorugh ye walles whan haue thē broke troyans ſo cruelly wroke fynally lefte none lyue ſlee kylle blyue walles theyr baners haue ſette yonge olde myght bette goth wracke vpon troye ſyde ne wyll lenger byde treaſoure golde may fynde caſte hepe togyder bynde make ſpoyle within haſte walles begyn pynacle toures alſo dungeowne brenne hewe bete downe ſoyle made euen playne great pray anone went agayne theyr ſhyppes glad lyght chere whan fyre flawmes clere caſtell conſumed ybrent auyſe prudent manly man worthy agamenon let make anone conuocacyon grekes bad ſhulde brynge golde treaſour without tariynge praye wanne tenedowne preſence concluſyowne may make diſtribucyon amonges without excepcyon lyke theyr deſert vnto pore ryche departeth euery man lyche moſte ſuche dyde beſte diſſerue hymſelfe hym lyſte thynge conſerue hath leuer theyr hertes gode ſuche hadde ſpente theyr owne blode manfully caſtell wynne largeſſe firſte begynne ne fayleth nat well ſpede thorugh helpe men whan hath nede loue foloweth fredome comenly ¶how kynge agamenon aſſembled baron grece afore kepe counſayle ſent vlixes kynge dyomede kynge pryamus meſſage ca xix kynge let make cry kyngꝭ lordes oſte duke erles come euery coſte nexte morowe tofore hym appere nyght ypaſſed phebus gan clere hir emyſperye larke ſonge whan y• kynge amonge grekes ſtronge vpon playne ſee royall faſte moſte chefe pryncypall lordes ſet theyr degre whan kynge ſawe oportunyte made ſcylence euery lyeges ſtandynge enuyron kynge chere ſad eke iocounde ſpeche full faucounde began tale ſobre countenaunce effect whiche ſubſtaunce syres quod full worthy degre right neceſſyte compelled bothe hye lowe myght lyke ye well knowe redreſſe thynge amys thorugh worlde reported force power myght worthyneſſe euery wyghtes ſyght moſte renowmed moſte worſhypable ydempt iuged moſte able people lyklyeſt ſtonde parforme take honde euer grutcheth ſayth nay yer ſemeth pay thylke power moſte acceptable vnto goddes lengeſt ſtondeth ſtable deuoyde ſurquedry pryde kouth vpon euery ſyde eche lande bothe one many harmes greues haue befall thorugh rancoure oonly pryde wylfulneſſe inportable coude expreſſe thorugh pryde done offence hye goddes make reſiſtence tho ſurquydous whiche vyce ſo contraryous may place abyde good fayth manhode pryde hath acqueyntaunce outher frendſhyp alyaunce proude man confederate hym herte hye lowe eſtate nedes muſte euer many neceſſyte lothſome firſte enmy contrayre thynge may man ſo moche appayre pryde ſothe hye lowe degre wherfore rede playnly foule vyce herte arrace quarell may haue grace ſpecyally dedes conueyed euer fall rightwyſneſſe volunte trouthe ſothfaſte guyde v directe rightfull lyne quarell ſhall aye honour ſhyne contune full felycyte ferthermore knowe ye come vengeaunce frendſhyppe alyaunce vpon pryam wronges done olde hym haue ofte tolde vpon haue grounde ytake ſome maked wake manfull hande caſtelles ſtronge ibete downe ſtonde haue ſo longe take rycheſſeꝭ founde ſlewe men many blody wounde harmes mo done countre wote well theyr enmyte vnto v great moche afore dare ſaye double auenged myght v echone anone ye ſhulde ſe theyr great ire ſo cruell ſo huge execute without refuge yet ſothe wote haue eſpyed beynge though nat aſkyred yet dare ſaye vtterly well ware faſte ouer wote well alſo harmes haue whiche yet freſſhe grene ſtronge myghty ſuſtene werre v anone wolde gynne yet cyte whiche inne walled ſtronge toured rounde aboute wene fully doute meyne haue gadred theyr alyes ſhall nat wyn ſmale werre ſtryfe ſothe hath prerogatyfe auauntage countre hym ſelfe diffendeth namely ſtuffed ſtronge frendes hym beſyde alyes dothe abyde lyke rauen fethers blake within neſt wyll ofte tyme make agayne faukon gentyll nature full harde diffence whyles may dure vaynquyſſhed outrayed yet ſome whyle faukon delayed whyles rauen beſyde neſt doth flee within courte lyberte euery foule frowarde areſte daunted owne neſte yet theſe wordes nat ſaye wyſe put fraye knyghtly herte ſo manly ſo ſtable ſhulde doutabſe troyans ſhall confounde theyr cyte whiche habounde playnely deſtroye albe ſtronge amonge shall fynally conſumpt dethe thorowe grekes ſwerde yelde vp brethe ¶but cauſe without drede ſaye thus ye take hede pryde preſumpcyon aduerte diſcrecyon prudently reaſon nede haſte may brydell lede ſo ordayne henſe wende laude prayſe ende may reported haue deuyſed many man hath nat aduyſed purſuyte lacke prouydence ſe tofore aduertence ſhuld falle deth hath brought suche wylfull haſte good thought v afore examynacyon well diſcuſſed reuolucyon ¶of thynkynge ofte nat repente firſte remembre pryam ſente v late oonly exyon yet holde kynge thelamon whiche v without aduyſement vndiſcretely denyed aſſent whiche hath v none aduauntage grounde rote full great damage thorugh wyſe purueaunce hir hadde made delyueraunce harmes great eſchewed parys ſo purſewed temple cythera buylde beſyde eirrea treſoure great alſo hadde iewelles hym ladde troye great rycheſſe ſlaughter men heuyneſſe yet made quene eleyne thorughoute grece great payne menelay hadde ben vnwrought hadde ſene thought wyſely afore exyon reſtored hadde nat harmes ſo mourned v echone ſoth faſtneſſe ſpent laboure ſo ydelneſſe treſoure good waſted ſo vayne come ſo ferre fetche agayne quene eleyne coſtes inportable withouten harmes eſchewable yet ne wote whether ioye aduerſyte thynge ſhall tourne aboute syth ofte ſythe dependent doute fatall thynge vnſyker vnſtable fro gynnynge ofte varyable ende ſene fortune tranſmewe hir gery cours therfore eſchewe harmes lykly poſſyble fall counſayle amonge vpon trauayle trauayle eſchewe mater ſewe pryamus without ſende firſte agayne reſtore quene eleyne right reaſon harmes done eke parys treſpas offency iuſtely make reſtytucyon may worſhyp honour retourne home without labour aſſente requere axynge lyſte nat folyly theyr wylfulneſſe refuſe worthyneſſe double aſſured aſyker grounde iuſte tytle troyans confounde thynges two ſhalbe vnder pyght firſte power borne vp ryght shall v fyght quarell dareyne balaunce weye atwixe v weyne fyne ſhalbe excuſed tofore haue wylfully refuſed oure iuſte profers made afore ſhalbe thorugh worlde therfore without ſpot treſpas blame myſreport hyndrynge name folye ſhall ynoted wylfull wodeneſſe playnely shall ſtande free power vſe euery man ſhall v well excuſe though execucyon takynge vengeaunce offencyon man childe eche ſect age ſhall deth holde paſſage ſwerde without mercy pace one better grace bvt yet tofore counſayle take hede ye meſoure bede holde beſte mooſt ſykerneſſe worke good auyſeneſſe amonge ſelfe lenger tarye whiche counſayle ſome contrarye varyaunt oppynyon saue mooſt diſcrecyon aſſented playnely ende choſen haue pryam ſende amonges embaſſy ſpede wyſe vlixes worthy dyomede whiche anone gan redy make ſhope forthe theyr way take towarde troye lyne ryght whan ſonne ſhone full ſhene bryght holdynge courſe firy ſpere mydday arke wonder bryght clere gylte eche hylle vale playne roche bemes whan dyde approche walles gate towne go without noyſe ſowne full well • eſene porte hadde right manfully way ladde paleyes ſtreyght lyne nedeth nat aſyde declyne court large wyde ſquare ful knightly wyght wold ſpare vnto effecte manly procede theyr charge without fere drede entre nat refuſed tho dayes paraunter nat vſed haue conduyte embaſſatrye cuſtome man denye ſuppoſe entre paſſage ſo come meſſage court buylded ſo ryally whan come meruayled full greatly royall ſyght ſo huge ſtrengthe well complete bothe brede lengthe nat hadde theyr lyfe fore sene none ſo fayre yet wonder paleyes togyder gone paued iaſper ſtone tree amyddes ſtode loke thought dyd thē gode muſynge artifycyall erect ſette magyk naturall engyne werkemen coryous thorugh ſubtyll craftes ſuperiticyous werke nygromancye profounde caſtyuge phyloſophye apparence illuſyon outher crafte incantacyon vp downe caſte theyr mynde reaſon coude fynde rote grounde wonder werke trouthe ſo derke theyr wytte though longe trace pryuyte compace conceyue poſſyble eye vyſyble ſothe without fable mannes hande ſo palpable whiche ſtocke guydo tolde ſoth faſtneſſe pured golde whiche ſhone bryght ſomer ſonne enlumyne thynges donne body maſte ryght proporcyoned mooſt goodly ſyght subſtancyall huge ſtrengthe twelue cubytes body lengthe croppe rounde large brede compas gan ſo flouryſſhe ſprede playne aboute enuyrowne bowes ſhadowed vp downe ryche braunches leues fayre twayne twayne ioyned payre one golde nother ſyluer ſhene meynt amonge wt ſtones whyte grene rede ſome ſapher hewed euery daye blomes renewed bloſſomes many ſondry fuyte ſtones ynde bare ſtede fruyte ſayth guydo ferther telle grekes wyll lenger dwalle holde theyr way many ſondry went parfourme fyne theyr entent tyll atteyne chambre pryncypall pryamus ſee royall lyke eſtate full kyngly wyſe sat aboute full prudent full wyſe lordes ſettes hym beſyde whan grekes ſurquedous pryde ſterne frowarde coūtenaunce lytell remembraunce gentylleſſe curteſye guydo doth playnely ſpecyfye entrynge taken haue theyr place oppoſyte kynges face ſet downe without ſermon obeyinge ſalutacyon worſhyp honour reuerence done kynge excellence pretudyce gentylleſſe anone vlixes gan expreſſe cauſe theyr comynge kynge pryamus without abode ſayinge euen thus nat forberynge preſence kynge oeruayle nat haue wondrynge though y• ne honour dewe comynge ſalewe syth ne longeth ſothe thynketh rancour hertely enmyte dedely hate ſalutacyons fayned falſe affeccyons ſhewe hertes fyre naturally man ſhall deſyre enmye helthe welfare platly lyſte nat ſpare shortly ſhewe fyne entent lyke haue cōmaundement meſſage agamenowne noble kynge mooſt worthy reuowne whiche v hath ſent ſeyne vnto quene eleyne rauyſſhed grekes lande brought troy force myghty hāde agaynſt right vyolence wherfore ſhortly without offence iuſtely axe without demaunde thou anone rightfully cōmaunde menelay ſhe ſent agayne axe nat vayne thou make reſtytucyon wronges done regyon pylfres great ſlaughter roberye parys done wylfull tyrannye whiche thy ſone ſuſteyned errour wrongefully meynteyned wherfore come fully condeſcende without grutchynge wronges amende ſo thou mayſte beſte goddes queme lyke thou myght thy reaſon deme right requereth worke wyſe ſo thou deſpyſe execute haue tolde truſte right well leſſon thou ſhalt lere whiche thou thyne ſhall ſore rewe without feynynge thou ſhalt fynde trewe thou better ende make cruell vengeaunce ſhall take fynally ſhulde fayne force deth quarell ſhall darayne vpon vpon blode raunſomles golde gode queſtyonles reporte mercyles ryche ſtronge cyte shall downe bete ylayde full lowe walle toures alſo ouerthrowe ſome well aduyſed axynge nat deſpyſed wyſely werke haue ſayde ſodaynly kyng pryamus ī abrayde haſty ire myght nat abyde grekes whan ſawe pryde great outrage preſumpcyon without abode dely beracyon • lixes anone gan breke vnto hym euen thus ſpeke wonder greatly myn aduertence beunge aſtoned ye preſence vngoodly dare make demaunde lyke ye hadde power cōmaunde conſtrayne byddynge obeye fere durſte nat ſaye maner thynge ye axe contrarye ye requyre wherof ſothly herte ameued thretes inwardly agreued aſtoned ſurely nat alyte ye bolde ſo excyte vylaynouſly myn honour prouoke wordes worke truſte right wele wyll nat paſſe boundes neuer adele rather ſhrotely ende axynge thynge condeſcende ¶for conſyder fyne entent nat ſyttynge conuenyent akynge graunte axynge thoughe y• stode myſchefe captyuyte without recure vttraunce bought outrage playnely thought axe hym ye axe ſothely yet ſuppoſe nat ye accomplyſſhynge may ſo moche auayle ye haue ſayde plately ye ſhall fayle purpoſe ſaye god toforne mauge myght though ye ſworne requeſt euery wyghtes ſyght wanteth grounde bothe trouthe ryght axe ſatiſfaccyon ſelfe firſte occaſyon whan ye ſlewe fader lamedowne lyeges brent eke towne many harmes ſought hym cauſeles ye wrought longe reherce whiche daye daye thorugh herte perce ſuſter eke called exyon ye ladde awaye regyon whiche nat vnto hir worthyneſſe ytreted lyke gentylneſſe ¶and ye wolde amendes haue wrongly whylom ſaue thynge pea ſtynte werre ſente grece ferre oonly haue hadde exyona agayne whiche ſonde ye hadde diſdayne cruelly vngoodly wyſe meſſager ye gan deſpyſe vnneth myght eſkape awaye grece ye knowe naye hadde ſo vngoodly chere good fayth lyſte nat requeſt gyue audyence axynge great offence leuer hadde ſhortely deye condeſcende ought ye ſeye wyll fully concluſyon knowen agamenon haue leuer douteles fynally werre pee syth ye haue done ſo great treſpace trouthe ſelfe place cruelly anone ye ſhulde dye offyce embaſſatrye agaynſt deth fully defence ſo bolde without reuerence preſence ſo threte ſpeke truſte right ſhulde one bewreke wherfore haſte without wordes mo counſayle ye go ſyght voyde cyte thus ſtandeth whyles ſe herte may entre gladneſſe fret ire put ſuche diſtreſſe good fayth may nat ſuſtene portune rage tene inwardly byndeth whyle dyomedes tho began ſmyle ſayde anone thus vnto kynge ſo thou comynge thyne herte haſte ſo moche payne v beholde buttwayne art therwith ſo inly ſette fyre ſhalt thou neuer without yre thy lyfe deuoyde woo sythe thou haſt ſo many cruell foo grekes entred thy lande hondred thouſande almoſte thyn hande agayne whoſe myght thou mayſt y• nat aſſure reſyſte playnely endure conſyder well ſtronge thou ſhalt wyt paraunter aught longe somanly men ſo well arayed expert armes olde aſſayed diffence many agayne vayle wyteeke well thou mayſt nat fayle deth ſwerde theyr hande deye thyne ſeye though ſo proudely thou ſpeke thy tunge oonly wreke afermeſt thou mayſt acheue better ſuche wordes leue wyſe counſayle take better hede haſte agayne dyomede surquydous moſte full pryde roſe vp ſome kynges ſyde ſwerdes drawe hym haue fall hewe amonge haſty ire brennynge glede tyll pryamus gan take hede roſe hym vp ſeynge diſeaſe manfully rage gan appeaſe diffendynge vpon deth lyfe none hardy ſtryfe embaſſatoures harme greue though fole foly wyll nat leue preſume ſpeke vnconnyngly wyſe man muſte ſuffre pacyently thoughe happe offence thorugh foly ſpeche lacke ſapyence wyſe man ne iongeth ſothe ſayne take hede ſpeke agayne fole perteynent ſhewe foly right ſo conuenyent wyſe ſothly ſuffraunce port haue tolleraunce foles longeth kyndely without aduyſe ſpeke folyly vndiſcretely menynge fulfylle wyſe man ſhall beſtylle tyll ſe tyme haue pacyence diſſymule aduertence rage foles laſt throwe tunge fole ofte knowe leuer hadde well aſſure perſone damage endure ſuffre meſſagere court haue wronge outher great lyte ſwerde rancour may nat alway byte vengeaunce thynge nought ofte falleth wronge wrought lytell exceſſe foloweth great reprefe haſte ayemedled myſchefe wherfore bydde ye ſytte downe wyſe preſumpcyowne attempteth nat maner wyſe ſygne worde deſpyſe embaſſatoures grekes ſent lette freely declare theyr entent ye whyles kepe lyppes cloſe ſodaynely eneas roſe whiche next kyng haue thā ſee inwardely rancour fret ne myght hymſelfe nat refrayne ſayde ſyr ſo ye nat diſdayne ſhall ſaye ſemeth well accordynge whan one hath ſayde amys rekleſly ſpoken vnaduyſed folye chaſtyſed may example hym take well ware ſuche noyſe crye make ſpecyally open audyence offende toyall excellence ſothely yet wote well myght gouerne playnely ſyght haſtyneſſe without aduyſement ſhulde cōmaundement deth deſerue great offence trewely yet ne preſence twayne haue ſo yſpoke without abode ſhulde anone wroke worthy right well ſyttynge whan fole preſence kynge bolde hardy preſumpcyon take hym indiſcrecyon thynge reherce concludynge ſentence preiudyce magnyfycence taught better gouerne large tunge konne bet diſerne whan ſhall ſpeke whan peſe ſuffre hym renne leſe doth ſpoke hath ſo large wherfore haſt counſayle hym charge without abode worde mo ſyght anone go beſte hym rede anone ful proudly dyomede nat aſtoned ſterne loke eneas yre quoke anſwered agayne wordes fewe ſayde ſyr thy wordes doth well ſhewe ſo thou thou art right wyſe well kynge doth thyne aduyſe hath nye counſayle ne may erre degre art ſo rightfull thy iugement wylfulneſſe without aduyſement cauſea lorde bondes pace wolde god ſome place myght fauoure fortune mete leyſer oportune lyke deſyre canſt ſo well endyte olde fable thy labour quyte thanke thy gentyll whiche ſo knyghtly thou haſt v ſhewed truſte well therto haue therof drede tho vlixes dyomede gan interrupte wordꝭ prudently hym ſayde full aduyſely beſte ſtynte ſtyll knowe fully wyll quod vlires full manly kynge wyll go henſe without tariynge thy ſyght agamenon make hym playne relacyon thy anſwer ordre horſe went ſodaynly ſhorte tyme ſo haſt theyr waye come ſaye kynge ſatte tentorye worde worde came memorye reherce ſubſtraunce euery dele wherof grekes lyke thynge wele conceyuynge full remedye reporte embaſſatrye saue oonly vtterly procede ſhall gouerne nede agayne troyans neceſſyte well wot may none aſſented wyll bede purueye faſte ſpede ſtorye ſhall fynde bvt make therof mynde muſte whyle eneas endyte myn auctor lyſt hym wryte whiche ſothly bokes ſaye manly troyan famous eneas anchiſis ſone great wortyneſſe whylom gete venus goddeſſe conqueroure many regyon whan troye brought deſtruccyon wente waye large ſee called tyrene ſaylynge forth goth many coſte many narowe paſſage many daunger tyll cartage ryued ſegan ſayle conqueſt great ytale ſo rome hath way take whoſe ofſprynge auctours make came auguſtus ceſar emperour whylom ſo noble conquerour renowne daye doth ſhyne enee emperour iuſtyne boke called autentykes full playnely wryt therin rubrykes ceſar ſo ceſares named yet right ſo eneades enee name ſhulde bere whiche fro troye comen ſo fere vnto ytayle eneas haue tolde ceſar deſcended downe lyne right full manly royall firſte rome ſceptre imperyall mauge theyr myght gouernaunce wyſoome ſette gouernaunce comon thynges touchynge cytee procede ferther enee hooly lyfe knyghthode ye lyſte rede ceryouſly ye maye ſe full autentyke ſtyle eneydos compyled virgyle albe ſo noble clerke graue afore complete werke bokes olde make mencyon ¶how kynge agamenon ſent achylles thelephus yle meſſa vitaylles ſlewe kynge made lephus kynge deth ca xx bvt nowe agayne agamenon without ſtyle wyl retourne whiche kynge wyll ſoiourne mater delayes make haſte hath counſayle take lordes beynge preſent ſuche nat hath ſent one erlys duke kynges ſayde ſyres amonge thynges iourney neceſſarye counſayle lenger tarye firſte make ordynaunce one aſſent prudent purueaunce alder firſte ſhape vytayle without whiche none hooſt may auayle parforme iourney thryftely wherfore rede faſte lykynge pleſaunce yle full habundaunce called meſſa ſende anone one worde aſſented euerychone choſen haue worthy achylles geleffus ſone hercules execute purpoſe fynally many worthy theyr company choſen thorugh hooſt anone achylles meſſa gone whiche lande ryche plenteuous reygned kynge worthy famous tentran hyght whiche tranquyllyté without werre aduerſyte hadde holde sceptre royall ſete yle ſo pleſaunt ſo mete albe ſome ſaye lytell yle kyngdome longeth cecyle hath name gyuen plente meſſane huge great cyte full plenteuous ſee lande whiche kyngdome vnderſtande ſayde meſſana meſſes latyne thorugh habundaunce fruyt corne wyne aryuayle playnes large wonte ſtuffe charge marchaunt ſhyppes ſtraunge fer countree thyder ſayle large ſee fetche vytaylle aye fro yere yere fro many coſte landes fer nere oonly eſchaunge march aundyſe eke alſo bokes deuyſe guydo full playnely telleth v kynge called meſſanus countre firſte meſſa toke name tyme great fame paſſynge ryche wonder plenteuous dare frygyus boke maketh mencyon ſhortly telleth concluycon howe achylles thelephus alſo meſſana togyder go thre thouſande grekes choſen oute moſte manly men amonges theyr route whiche faſte gan londe kynge gan vnderſtonde theyr comynge deſcended downe worthy regyowne ou hors fote ſtele armed bryght agaynſt grekes manfully fyght deuoyde playnely ye ſodaynely thus ſkarmyſſhe gan wyxe grekes theyr mortall fone outher parte many one slayne hurte deth ywounded euer vnlyckely therof ſounded hor treate none atwene ſwerdes ſharpe ſperes ſquare kene go grounde euery man foo confounde laboure dyde beſyneſſe though grek thrugh theyr worthyneſſe hadde theyr foo • moche lande ywonne yet reſorte begonne meruayle none bycauſe theyr fone hadde alway thre noumbre agaynſt one tyme may none tyll achylles gan beholde ſe mortall ſlaughter vpon grekes ſyde tournynge backe wt woūdes large wyde haſty rancour chaunge gan blode ire furyous wode whan behelde men leſe theyr lande y• ſwerde whiche helde hande made waye kylled bare downe felde lyke fyers lyowne fared ſothe whan men ſlawe makynge foon backwarde withdrawe grekes ſo manly recomforte maugre made reſorte euer way ſtode without mercy kylleth mode gayneth nat cruelte douteles ne manhode paſſynge renowne worthyneſſe knyghthode eke hye proweſſe grekes hadde daye fynallye vaynquyſſhed without remedye thorugh helpe recure achylles ſturdy wall gan ſerche ſheltrouns theyr rangys brake fore whoſe face fomen go wrake alderlaſte whan gan eſpye tentran kynge thorugh chyualrye diffende hymſelfe lyke worthy knyght lyon bare hym fyght grekes ſo oppreſſe achylles cruell hardyneſſe ne wolde ceaſe putſewynge thorugh warde tyll came kynge manly force ſtoute full pryde makynge awaye rounde euery ſyde agayne whoſe myght thyng myght auayle tentran firſte auentayle raced hath rente mayle ſonder hewe wonder conſydre day cruelte broke hath baſſenet many cruell wounde myght ſmyt kynge grounde haſte maked hath lette hede rende baſſenette mercyles vengaunce harme gan heyghte auaunce fully purpoſe ſhall dede raunſomles gan hamyn hede blody ſwerde deſpytous herte caſtynge playnely ſhuld hym nat aſſerte ire ſo furyous ¶but fortune befell right thus thelephus yonge luſty knyght caſuelly therof hadde ſyght achylles maner full behelde ſtroke anone bare vp ſhelde gan achylles mekely preye haue pyte ſo hym deye syth lay wounded almoſte deth brought poynt yelde vp breth beſechynge hym benyngnyte manly routhe knyghtly eke pyte withdrawe hande hym grace graunte hym lyfe lytell ſpace syth euery knyght ſhulde gentylleſſe enmye ſpare whan diſtreſſe vttraunce brought ſpecyally whan mercy requyreth humble volunte achylles feruent yre rancoure ſette fyre anſwerde agayne lyſt ſo preye hym nolde pryde wyll obeye gan werre nede diſdayne indignacyon hauynge truſte preſumpcyon manhode myght hy nat auayle agaynſt grekes holde batayle preuyd playnely ende otherwyſe ſhortly wende dyche iuſtely falle whiche made malys v alle ¶where wyll entencyon gaue vnto hym none occaſyon vpon ſyde platly fer nere mynyſtred hym matere londe mente damage hymſelfe grounde rage without offence done hym v efte agayne yonge thelephus humbly requyred achylle knyghtly routhe axynge fulfylle haue mercy hym ca fader kynge whylom quod thelephus bonde conferate whiche lyeth deſconſolate expectant oonly dedely face vpon houre whan goſte ſhall pace thorugh gyrte ala wt many mortall woūde cauſe haue hym founde afore tyme full great kyndeneſſe manhode gentylleſſe boundes regyowne vnto thorugh hye renowne whylom caſuelly gan ryde shewed ſothe vpon euery ſyde full ryall chere great humanyte bounde duyte remembre haue mynde douteles elles vnkynde whiche wolde name foule twyte parcell wolde hym quyte beſeche reſpyte lyfe achylles without ſtryfe delyuered hath ſtorye telleth thus tentran frely vnto thelephus whether hym lyſte ſaue ſpylle whan hym wylle conſydered woundes grene ſo mortall ſothely ſo kene nede muſte dye gayne remedye auayle may medecyne hour whā phebꝰ weſtward gan declyne batayle brought ende whyle grekes theyr ſhyppes wende meane whyle tentran payne woundes gan complayne without ſtaunche ſo pyteouſly blede offycers faſte gan ſpede lytter made full royall towarde paleys doūge owne pryncypall cary hym ſoftely eaſely ¶and prayer full benyngnely thelephus alſo achylles conueyed hym amonges prees tyll brought lyſte receyued lyke theyr degre full royally kynge aye languyſſhynge drewe towarde endynge myght nat lenger drawe lengthe wofull lyfe ſo weke ſtrengthe ſpirite muſte algates wende haſte made ſende achylles thelephus whan came ſayde vnto thus syres quod full worthy degre helthe honour longe proſperyte vnto good aduenture whyle lyfe may dure ſpecyally thelephus whiche haſte ſo gracyous gentylleſſe paynes ſtronge oonly grace lyfe prolonge deth ala may nat eichewe ſwerde part remewe without recure knytte bytter bondes vpon brynke falle fatys hondes lyfe fully deſpeyre whiche body neuer myght haue heyre daye ſucceſſyon gouerne lytell regyon whiche lyckely ſtande deſolate gouernaunce diſconſolate whiche wan wt full great trauayle day werre batayle haue kepte ye well knowe echoue defended maner fone without loſſe yeres toforne recurlees yore lorne ne helpe eke ſocour hercules great conquerour whylom fader thelepus ſtronge ſo myghty ſo chyualrous whoſe manhode whoſe hardyneſſe knyghthode great worthyneſſe whiche day day newe memorye foon hadde victorye daunted made ſo ferde oonly rygoure ſharpeſwerde fynally thorugh manly hede made reygne poſſede maugre theyr myght pea quyete ſeptre crowne royall ſete none tyll dede hardy lyfte vp hede agaynſt ſpeke wordes fewe wherby may fully declare ſhewe euydence lytell yle perteynent longeth cecyle hercules memoryall • tte pylers conqueſt royall whan hadde ryde go fere columpna yet name bere hym called herculea though ſome ſaye hyght herracula name chaungynge corrupcyon whiche lande whylom manſyon people wylde barbarye whiche kyngdome magnefye frederyke ſothly ſecounde golde good paſſyngly habounde choſen emperour rome towne myghty gouernour whylom eke kynge cecyle whiche made reyſe large yle myghty toure hye thycke walle ſayth guydo memoryall put name longe remembraunce ſoyle pleſaunce floures freſſhe many ſondry hewe ſome bokes londe named newe pealled vnderſtonde fayreneſſe luſty newe londe tentran aye lymge payne faſte gan houre attayne cruell deth afore lordes made haſte thelephus call preſence mortall chere sayde openly myght ſone quod nowe ſhall pace worlde gayne may grace lyfe ſaue thorugh mannes myght bycauſe equyte ryght compelled iuſtly ſentence declare elerely conſcyence fore deth herynge prees ſage thy fader hercules wyſe worthy knyghtly man whylom londe thorugh conqueſt wan whiche oonly goodly hede ſtocke manly hede toke vnto cōmyſſyon gouernaunce regyon free wyll hole regallye nolde hymſelfe cowne occupye ſothely yet right nat laſſe loue ſhall paſſe withall entent laſte wylle graunt ryght ſkylle heyer iuſtely ſuccede longe honour therin thy lyfe lede makynge prodeſtacyon full token confirmacyon wyll fynall myn herte fro whiche man may dyuerte vpon ſyde vtterly declyne hor firſte wyll diſſent lyne togyder combyne one whiche thynge mortall man may gone deſyre laſte langour thou playnely succeſſour fynally thus conclude deme vnto septre dyademe delyuered euery circumſtaunce wyll aſſuraunce made wryte teſtament fyne concludynge laſte entent full pyteouſly thelephus beſought hertely manly routhe knyghtly gentylleſſe deuer beſyneſſe deth lyke eſtate royall halowe holde feſte funerall solempnely exequyes ſodaynely without wordes mo kynge tentran yeldeth vp goſte went way note coſte nat deme ſuche myſtyhede whan parcas broken haue thrde rokke forth waye thelephus marbyll graye curyouſly tombe madekerue dede corp therin conſerue full rychely aboue graue epythaphe anone dyde graue honour playnely expreſſe knyghthode bothe worthyneſſe goſte deuorced letter ryche golde aboue enboced rounde aboute wonder curyous tombe ſayde playnely thus lyeth tentran kynge douteles whylom ſlayne cruell achylles ſceptre regalye hoolly gaue whiche man may denye thelephus ſone hercules whiche tombe reſteth pee whan perfourmed euery thynge thelephus crowned kynge hye lowe one aſſent openly parlement made fayth hym ydone homage lyke theyr degree age hole herte theyr beſt entent othe aſſured ſacrament trewe lyeges receyued hym kynge achylles without tariynge whan ſette pea gouernaunce without grutchynge varyaunce theyr ſhyppes anone made carye euery thynge neceſſarye grekes corne fruyte vytayle fleſſhe fyſſhe myght auayle hoſteynge helpe theyr nede downe ſee hedyde lede fully theyr veſſell ſtuffe lade thelephus made stylle boundes regyon abyde concluſyon thorugh helpe dylygence beſynes diſcrete prouydence agayne myſchefe ſcarſyte whan alle syttynge enuyron many worthy knyght ¶and firſte meſſa telleth fyght whan entred theyr welcomynge ceryouſly tolde eke kynge tentran hyghte playnely alſo howe achilles amydde ſelde hym ſlowe dethe hole entent fully ordeyned teſtament thelephus alſo heyre tolde eke • eyre vnto ſee eke vytayle thelephus wyll nat fayle ſende may pleaſe whiche thynge grekes great eaſe brought herte lyke wonder well whan achilles hadde tolde euerydell greatly preyſed hye prouydence manhode bothe ſapyence beynge bare hym ſo achilles go lodgynge lytell beſyde knyghtes vpon hym abyde myrundones full glade comynge hym receyued longeth kynge abode reſted hym whyle guydo declyneth ſtyle grekes troye towne muſte alſo make dygreſſy owne myne auctor ſteppes ſhewe lyke conuenyent dewe matere ſyth guyde whyle grekes called ly • ye came kynge glaucon • ith hym brought ſone spardon noble knyght armes full famous allyed kynge pryamus thre thouſande ſhall nat fayne came knyghtꝭ wt theſe lordes twayne larys ryche worthyneſſe fyue hondred dare telleth v came hupon epedus many knyghtes plate ſyluer bryght hym eke kynge y• remus hyght brought iij thouſande troye many myle tabaria large myghty yle duke foure theyr chyualrye 〈◊〉 erie viij came companye hauyngem armes great experyence bare without difference theyrmen whan y• felde chief golde eueryche ſhelde wherby kynge booly nauye amonge knowen myght bore eke ſame fro trace kynge pylex name fro thy • ke trace moſte excellent whiche plage oryent haueth ſyght frō myghty kȳ • ge thouſande knyghtꝭ brought comynge myne auctor recordeth eke alſo hondred knyghtes troye go alchamus duke eke full famous came pylex guydo wryteth thus troyans helpe theyr great nede fro pauonye ſothely rede came pretemeſſus noble werryour lorde lande kynge gouernour duke stupex hym eke hadde knyghtes thouſande ladde towarde troye regyon ſtorye maketh mencyon yle ſtandeth moſte wylderneſſe woodes plenteuous thyckeneſſe growe therin many full dyuerſe tree moſte foreſt men may ſe buylde houſes fewe lande full dyuerſely themſhewe many lykneſſe queynte monſtruous beſtes vnkouthe ſyghte meruaylous stoundemell apparence illuſyon falſe exiſtence wonder gaſtefull playnely ſene dyuerſe goodes woodes grene appere called satyrye cornys eke fawny incubye cauſe often men falle rage lande people full ſauage hardy knyghtes furyous wode deſyrous aye ſhede blode greatly experte ſpecially ſhete darte ſpere peryllous mete caſte euen lyne ile named botyne great arraye troye cyte lyke fynde came duke thre firſte called auphymyus saume ſecounde thirde forcyus ſayth dare whiche lyſte natlye twelue hondred knyghtꝭ theyr companye fro bytunye made remembraūce ryche lande hath ſuche habundaūce ſpyces gōmes fruytes corne wyne holſome rote ryndes ryche fyne wonder vnkouthe precious alſo whiche ile came knyghtes two full knyghtly men armes deſyrous kynge boetes epyſterus wt brought troye ſo ferre thouſande knyghtes arayed werre fro lande called paffogonye whiche ſeuered companye bokes ſaye hyſtoryall vnder plage oryentall sette ſo ferre made reherſayle fewe none lande trauayle come almoſte impoſſyble whiche lande called muyſyble bycauſe oonly remocyon ryche regyon golde ſyluer alſo ſtones habundaunte plente none ſo full treaſoure gode hath ſyght ryche flode named tygre nat fer eufrates ſayth myne auctour called dare fro whiche lande ſtele armed clene thouſande knyghtꝭ came phylymene worthy kynge whoſe ſheldes orede querboyl guydo rede golde depaynte fret ſtones ryche worlde trowe none lyche floodes choſen deuyſe whiche haue theyr courſe paradyſe whiche kynge gyaunt ſtature makynge paſſynge meaſure stronge delyuer alſo fynde fro lande marcheth vpon ynde kynge porſes came many knghtly man alſo honde hym wan moche honour noble meryon brother called sygamon whiche lande theyr ſubieccyowne duke erles knyghtes renowne thre thouſande brought plate ſhene ſperes rounde whet full quare kene ethyope came noble route kyngdome alſo doute teremo dare called came kynge full prudent full wy manly man named theſeus eke ſone hyght archylogus thouſande knyghtes theyr companye theſeus full nye allye pryamus diſcent blode kynges twayne paſſynge ryche gode renowmed knyghthode fame guydo reherſeth nat theyr name yet ſtorye maketh menſyon agreſta lytell regyon thouſande knyghtꝭ brought vnto troye grekes pryde daunte acoye choſen pycked ye none lande beyonde amazones lyſſyny kynge epyſtrophus wyſe ſo worthy inly vertuous paſſynge counſayle diſcrecyowne full worthy renowne preuyd alſo ſpecyall artys called lyberall lerned expert ryght natwithſtandynge worthy knyght werre pea manfull ryght ſage ron ferre age ſtorye maketh reherſayle thouſande knyghtꝭ cladde plate mayle troye towne fynde ladde hym guydo ſayth hadde wonder archer ſyght meruaylous fourme ſhap maner monſtruous lyke myne auctour reherce fro nauell vp warde man lower downe lyke hors yſhaped thylke parte man maked ſkynne blacke rough vere coueryd fro colde hym paſſynge foule horryble ſyght whoſe eyen ſparkelynge bryght furneys rede leuene ye lyghtenynge yt cometh downe fro heuene dredefull loke reed fyre • rede good archere bowe bothe euen morowe vpon grekes wrought moche ſorowe gaſtyd many hydous loke ſterne many quoke whan hym ſawe ſo ougly horrybly lothſome credyble many one hath wounded deth cauſed yelde vp breth grekes ſyde ye ſhall wyſe aſſembled yfere kynges duke erles renowne ſondry landes within troye towne gaderyd come fro ſo ferre ſayth dare helpe werre nombre maketh mynde two thurty thouſande fynde worthy knyghtes lordes eſtate fythe worlde fourmed create ne ſene trowe one cyte togydre aſſembled ſo hye degre knyghtes ſo great multytude yet dare ſothly conclude boke maketh nomynde came troye ſmaler ynde nouther moſte famous renowne wt pryam yborne troye towne fynally trewely ſought syth houre world wrought dare afferme vnder phebus ſpere many worthy nat mette yfere manly men flourynge luſtyneſſe freſſhe ſo yonge lyklyneſſe euery poynt ſhape arraye well ſothely naye lyſte conſyder vpon outher ſy • e thorugh worlde men go ryde th • floure knyghthode worthyneſſe chyualrye hye proweſſe aſſembled withoute within fully aſſented werre begyn ¶wherfore ye lyſters take good hede delyte boke rede firſte lytell werre began lyght y• cauſe whiche ſo many man hath loſte lyfe myſchefe pytuouſly yet man beware therby almoſte nought ſtryfe begonne lyſt loke haue thyng wonne oonly deth ala harde ſtounde many knyght caught dethes wounde withoute recure remedye woman ſhall nat lye gan ſtryfe pyte ſo great myſchefe aduerſyte mortall ſlaughter euer ſhulde tyde better haue ſette aſyde suche quarelles dere ynough myte let paſſyd vengeaunce byte wyſedome caſte afore ſe ſuche ſklaundres myght eſchewed venym gonne rype though y• men horne blowe pype whan hous fyred hete ſparcle late trete cauſed wherfore gynnynge remedy put euery thynge euery wyght may deme reaſon whyle grekes lay tenedon refreſſhe reſte pe worthy kynge called pallamydes thurty ſhyppes grekes lande stuffed wt knyghtꝭ ful worthy theyr hande beſte choyſe regyon aryued vp tenedon wherof grekes whan ſyght reioyſynge right glade lyght hauynge rewarde vnto worthyneſſe afore hadde heuyneſſe abſence ſo longe ſome grutched hym ſtronge nat kepte mouſtre athene ſhewe clene ſpotte conſcyence full manfully open audyence lyke knyght hegan hymſelf excuſe stoppynge tho theron lyſte muſe abſence ſhe wynge cauſe ſykeneſſe ſodayne malady cōſtrayned preſence withdrawe ſawe lykenſſe hath lawe helde excuſed fully abſence moſte reuerence amonge grekes wyght ſecounde alſo full wyſe eke habounde golde good auyſe prudent ſo euer ſette entent knyghtly wyſely wolde aye well acheue gan ne wolde leue maugre foon maner wyſe tyll ſawe fyne empryſe moſte oppynyon amonge grekes reputacyon hym • ought wolde theyr counſayle auyſely toſe euery maner thynge aſſenteth vnto theyr axynge benygnely gentylneſſe grekes dyde theyr beſyneſſe procede without delaye enhaſte euer maye gynne ſege differre nought ſondry wayes ſerched haue ſought theyr wyttes fro tenedowne maye remeue towarde troye towne hauen theyr ſhyppes ſome thought moſte cōmodyte moſte expleyt nyght pryuely towarde troye ſtode faſte proudely ſayle theyr ſhyppes alle ſome ſayde great peryll myght falle towarde nyght take ſee leſt derkeneſſe ennoſed bee theyr paſſage knowynge nat waye wherof great harme falle maye thus dyuerſe oppynyon procedynge nat concluſyon effect theyr purpoſe nat ne helde ſtyll lye aye lodged felde lyke entryked drede tyll daye worthy dyomede grekes ſeynge cowardyſe euen thus counſayle gan deuyſe syres quod preſent ye lyſte one aſſent goodly conſydre aduertynge prudently ſhall ſaye tofore openly whiche knyghthode haue ſo noble name sothly ſemeth ought haue gret ſhame whiche holde ſelfe ſo myghty ſo ſtronge lande ſoiourned haue ſo longe nygh yere durſte wyſe remeue henſe cowardyſe haue nat ellys certaynely foon graunted folyly euen theyr luſte ſpace lyberte make ſtronge opportunyte v withſtande playnely hande ſo wyll ye may well vnderſtande ¶for day day confuſyowne ſought wayes full wyſely vp downe gette helpe mene ſpace enforced aboute euery place theyr large cyte barrerys palys theyr wall maſcued agayne ſkalys truſteth theron made great ordynaunce gouernaunce haue aſpyed ſeynge drede haue herte manly procede purpoſe holde werre aye ſe deferre wyll catche hardyneſſe v reſyſte theyr beſyneſſe alſo ſe truſte veryly hadde afore hande manfully began knyghtly forth contynued iourney hadde better fortuned ſodaynely ſtronge myghty hande vnauyſed hadde theyr lande without abode afore tyme aryued whiche whyle muſte depryued delayed firſte victorye honour palme glorye myght ſothely ne ſlouthe wyl complyſſhed playnetrouthe maugre v lande aryue ſtrōge defence wyl agayne v ſtryue put v ſtronde wynne aye tarye begynne ſothe lyſte nat lye put ſelfe echone ieopardye ſhulde fayne fage fro trouthe tariynge cowarde • louthe lykely tourne v great ſorowe wherfore erely tymes morowe counſayle ankers vp pulle mater lenger dulle enarme ſhyppes werre vp ryſe morowe ſterre lette v ordayne knyghtly apparayle hauen wynde ſayle manfull herte luſty freſſhe courage courſe holdynge right paſſage towarde troye lande oppedlye euer falle truſte ſykerlye without ſcarmouſſhe may nat aryue fro troye deſcende wyll blyue lyke manly men mete v berde lette v nat aferde voyde drede manhode ſette afore cowardyſe entre bore taſte manhode herte worde grekes gan aduerte manly counſayle dyomede effect procede dede vnto poynt nothynge ſpare wyſe anone ſhall declare ⸫ ⸫ ⸫ ¶how grekes toke lande troye ſtrongely fought ca xxi next morowe wonderly tyme phebus vp roſe lōge p̄me whan began full meryly dawe grekes hoſte ſhypwarde gan drawe manly herte fully deuoyde drede thorugh comforte dyomede alder firſte anone awoke lordes wyſely theyr counſayle toke concluded amonge euerychone whiche theyr ſhyppes ſhulde meſt gone ſee ſhulde guye aryue man aſpye deuyſed certayne marke nyght paſſed ſyngynge larke grekes ſhypped without tariynge bothe hye lowe dawnynge firſt tofore hondred ſhyppes toure stuffed many worthy warryoure gan proudely ſayle charge baners brode bryght large ſplayed vpon euery ſyde departed fomy wawes wyde ſyghte whelmen vp ſo grene next werre wel enarmed clene another hondred folowed faſte whiche bare theyr ſayles paſſyngly proudely ful many worthy knyght armed mayle plate bryght foloweth hoolly theyr nauye trowe ſuche companye worthy kynghtes lordes degree neuer afore ſene vpon ſee • olus fortunate eke neptune made none debate wt wynde trouble amōge ſterne wawes atempre weder full mery dawes tyde ſayled ryght troye towne caughte anone ſyght wherof herte full glade lyght whan troyans firſte theyr ſhyppes ſe proudely ſayle lytell fro ſtronde ſawe caſte londe bode arme haſtely plate mayle iackes rychely irous herte done anone toke theyr hors forth haſte gone gate made tariynge ne abyde prynce duke kynge lor • e guyde gouerne haſte forth ſo many ſo yerne torough felde ſo great multytude amonges folkes rude manly men thryftely ſayne clenly armed large playne whan grekes gan firſte beholde • nombre theyr hertes gan colde none ſo manly amonge yonge ſo freſſhe ſo hardy ſo ſtronge hye eſtate lowe degre ne ſtonyed ſe hardy troyans ſo proudly downe deſcēde lette grekes nat aſſende wyſte conceyue vtterly meane aryue knyghtly gan ſonde thylke daye lyke man founde many mortall wounde vpon troyans wrought wracke berynge downe fote horſe backe ire ſtrokes ſo kene whiche tyme worthy phylomene lorde kynge paffogonye whan behelde companye many troyan vlixes ſlawe tawardes hym anone gan hym drawe horſe backe ſpere rounde ſadell bare hym grounde vlixes roſe vp anone ryght takynge horſe lyke manly knyght whiche anone phylomene hath ſayne toke efte aſpere rode hym agayne myghtely ſuche vyolence fynally gayneth diffence ſmote hym euen thorugh y• ſhelde whiche flewe ſondre felde thorughe plate without fayle ſpere hede ran reſted mayle forged ſtele full ſhene bryght whiche perce ſpere hede hath myght trewely made hawberiowne ſtroke vlixes bore downe yet efte agayne vp roſe anone whiche ſtroke harme ne felte none raughte ſpere ſharpe whet grounde phylomene gaue ſuche wounde myght armes twayne irous herte ſo great payne thorugh ſhelde bothe place mayle ſmote hym vp thorugh auentayle gorge ſtocke gan glyde hors fell downe ſyde full perryllouſly pyght vpon hede knyghtes wenynge ſothly dede whiche toke hym vp layde hym ſhelde bare hym home haſte felde great daūger myght hym wȳne thorugh grekes theyr lorde twȳne troyans ſuppoſed ſykerly phylomene without remedy hadde deed aſtoned caſe day ne fall phyſomene grekes ſtronde •• dde outrayed aryuynge vp londe thorughe knyghthode douteles phylomene vlixes v • ho • ſed hath mortall wounde knyghtly wyſe troyans confounde wherof aſtoned euerychon ¶but tho agamenon greks ooſte lorde emperour aryued vnto theyr ſocour knyghtes menelaus eke worthy thelamonyous called ayax lande come leyſer haue theyr hors nome whyle grekes troyans occupye sor • fyghtynge gan faſte hye towardes makynge delay fruſſhe haſte may ran yfere theyr ſperes bracke herte enuyous vpon hors backe myght men worthy knyghtes ſe theyr ſtedes eche flee ſtyffe ſwerdes ſhaftes great rounde hedes ſquare poyntes kene grounde myght men ſe theyr furyous tene many knyghtes dede vpon grene moſte ſlaughter confuſyowne fell thylke tyme towne grekes ſo myghty ſo ſtronge felde contynueth longe tyll protheſilaus ſtronge myghty kyng whiche daye ſkarmyſſhe fyghtyng full lyke knyght occupyed agayne troyans cruelte manhode oonly worthyneſſe aduenture weryneſſe hym refreſſhe take eyre brethe hym maked repeyre ſtronde dyde aryue ¶where thought herte gan toryue cruell yre alfo pyte caughte oonly ſe men lye ſlayne ende longe ſtronde ſome comynge vp londe dreynt ſee amonge floodes depe whiche thynge gan anone wepe full pyteuoſly nat eſpyed whoſe wofull eyen myght nat dryed conſtreynt whiche ſat ſonye herte tyll laſte amonge paynes ſmerte cruell yre gan herte enbrace ſodaynely deſpytous face without abode thought vpon theyr deth wolde auenged fynally attones deye ſtede toke ryght weye towarde foon full irous rage lyne right holdeth paſſage swyfte grayhounde y• renneth lee ſawe gretteſt prees preceth thorugh amyddes felde wt ſwerde whiche hande helde grounde kerue byte full mortally aboute hym gan ſmyte troyans myght hym nat aſterte ryueth euen herte ſome woundeth ſothely deth ſome made yelde vp breth vnhorſeth ſome cruelly mette day vtterly hors made hym alyght rode fledde ſyght preſence deth eſchewe euer one gan ſewe chaſe lyke wood lyon playe playeth towne tyll perſeus ethyopye kynge ye cyte came ſodaynely rydynge many knyght many lyfely man whoſe comynge newe began freſſhe ſkarmyſſhe furyous woode many greke day loſte blode felle aſſaute troyans make amonge ethyopyes blake manly bare fyghtynge troyans afore fere 〈◊〉 newe aſſured y• thorugh theyr helpe haue y• felde recured made leſe alſo moche agayne tofore wonne playne ſo hole ſo myghtely kept togydre ſo auyſely gouerned pauys ſpere ſhelde grekes compelled felde maugre ſo grutche neceſſyte ſironde backewarde flee almoſte diſpayred mate comforteles whyle kynge pallamydes theyr reſcous come arryuayle luſty freſſhe entreth batayle knyghtes hole maynee takynge theyr hors faſte ſee full proudely enbuſſhed attones ſpere ſwerde ygroūde none conueyinge theyr worthy comynge haue ſo oppreſſed theyr comynge manly troyans wonder ſe lye ſlayne yonder contynueth tyll amonge prees auenture pallamydes brennynge aye furyoushete amyd felde happeth mete worthy knyght called sygamon whiche brother kynge menon 〈◊〉 alſo guydo doth reherce manly man kynge perce whiche grekes daye ſore opreſſed knyghthode expreſſed grekes worthyneſſe ofte brought full great diſtreſſe ſame daye great encrees • ut fortune ala pallamydes tolde hath felde hym mette aſpere ſquare ſharpe whette whan knyghthode moſt ī pryde rode hym ſmote hym thorugh y• ſyde laſte dedely fatall wounde ſtede bare hym grounde playne blode rede 〈◊〉 •• amydes lefte hym pale dede amonges troye forth rode bare downe euer waye ſtode ſo furyous wode maugre troyans tofore hym playne made reſorte walle agayne manly knyghtes alway faſte hym awaytynge full ententyfely redy honde euery great empryſe tho began noyſe aryſe wofull clamour pyteous crye troye whiche vtterly agayne grekes myght nat ſuſtene mortall ſwerde ſo ſherpe kene noble worthy famous knyght pallamydes great myght longe daye hath yborne hym ſo agayne foon ſo knyghtly perſone thorugh hye renowne chaced hath almoſte towne troyans echone manly made fle noyſe entred cyte hydous crye mortall ſhoute ¶wherof ameued ector yſſueth oute furyouſly
